go

A ruined reputation, and Cheng returning changed in the rain.

Chapter One: the beginning


Tapping her foot against the tiled floor of the high school class room, the brunette found herself almost growing attached to the melody her foot seemed to make against the flooring. Her English 4 teacher happened to be doing the same thing she did every other day, rambling about nonsense that had nothing to do with the class itself. This had her drifting off in her own day dreams, trying to imagine she was anywhere other than the place she actually was.

Previously, school wasn't something she'd dreaded much at all. She used to love it, in fact. Although, she wasn't ever one who was involved in the popularity clique and had bundles of friends, she had never been lonely when she was at school. For back then, she had the greatest friends a girl could've asked for.

To be more specific, by friends, it merely meant two people. Through out middle school and into sophomore year of high school, she'd had two amazing friends that helped her get through anything she faced. It's unfortunate to think how everything happened, she found herself sighing dully, wishing the tedious day away. The hard realization she now had no one wasn't something she found herself wanting to be stuck on.

The sudden drrr of the screeching bell was the highlight of her slow day. As if in unison, the sound of chairs against the tile was heard, and she - like every other student - shot to their feet, eager to get out of such a meticulous classroom. And like every other day, she received the multiple dirty looks from students as she threw her bag over her shoulder, making her way towards the exit of the room.

At this point, she found them almost humorous. Since the incident years ago, she'd come to face the fact there was nothing she could ever do to save her trashed reputation, so instead she embraced it with open arms. This is what she found herself doing as she threw the dirty looks right back at anyone who dared to shoot them towards her first.

It wasn't that she was rude in this sense, but more of the fact she stopped caring completely. Soon enough, she'd be graduating and thankfully never have to see any of the useless humans she attended high school with again. Therefore, she wasn't worried about what they thought. It didn't matter to her, especially if she knew it wasn't true.

Despite the looks she continued to get even as she was making her way towards the exit, casually keeping to herself like she always did, she held her head high. She never bothered anyone, and she never had. But the idiotic students in the school believed whatever they were told, and still managed to see her as some sort of monster. It was all false, but they'd never believe her, not when it was only her to say such. oh well, not much I can do about it.

Maybe Si Cheng isn't busy today, the thought floated into her brain as she adjusted the strap of her bag on her shoulder, diverting her eyes from the students that grimaced at her to her feet, thinking hard about the subject. She hadn't seen him in so long, and he was practically the only friend she had left on the face of the Earth. It sucked he'd moved schools, especially during Senior year, she wasn't even sure how long it'd been since she last saw him. Every time she called, he was 'super busy.'

Deciding she was most definitely going to contact her close friend, she was already pulling out her phone, searching through her contacts for the familiar name. Her green eyes were so focused on the screen she was paying absolutely no attention to where she was walking in front of her, but it wasn't like she needed to anyway. People practically parted like water when they'd see her coming. She wouldn't exactly mind it if she didn't know why.

Waiting till she was outside, the cold breeze that was blowing on that Wednesday afternoon pricked at her skin. Being she was wearing nothing more than a romper, goosebumps formed on her skin, but if anything, she welcomed them. Cold weather was her favorite, and as she diverted her eyes to the sky, growing distracted from her previous plan, the clouds seemed to be taking over the sun. Was it going to rain? God, I hope so.

Just the thought of the fact her favorite weather would be coming was enough to cause a close-lipped smile to spread across her lips. Looking back down to her phone, she went back to finding Si Cheng's number. This hadn't taken her long at all, and soon enough her finger was hovering over the contact named 'Chengie🐭.' Just seeing her old friend's grinning face in the contact photo seemed to make her day better, and she found herself anticipating hearing his voice as her finger hovered over the call button.

Completely oblivious to the fact there were other students walking down the sidewalk on their way home as well, she found herself almost bumping into people while debating with herself on calling him. She'd already decided she was going to, but when she was about to, she found herself growing nervous for reasons even she was unsure of.

Due to the fact she was in such deep thought, she'd almost jumped over a foot in the air at the sound of a car slowing down against the curb which she walked by, honking the horn. A hand flew to her heart as her eyes widened, wondering who had the audacity to do such a thing - especially to her. She was practically feared in the school, or more like everyone just hated her. So the thought anyone would suddenly want to converse was astonishing.

This is what she thought, until she'd looked up to see the familiar 2018 Audi. The fresh paint on the car was so shiny that despite the sun not being out to help it, it still hurt her eyes. Just seeing such a vehicle was enough for her to know, and she was only disgusted further as the exact person she assumed rolled down the driver's window.

That same ridiculous smile hung on his lips as his eyes met hers, "Hey cupcake, do you need a ride?"  his tone was deceitful, and she narrowed her eyes at him, before they'd directed to the others that sat in the front and back seat. To think of what he'd really turned into.

"No," the word was harsh as it fell from her lips. The other guys in the vehicle had made some sort of ooh sound from her hard rejection towards the boy, and she forced herself to look away from them and his look of defeat, turning on her heel and continuing to walk down the sidewalk.

She should've known she wasn't gonna get far. The screeching of the wheels were heard as he began to drive slowly by the curb at the same pace which she walked.

"Hey, Hye, I won't try anything, I'm just asking as a friend if you need a ride."

Her house was actually quite the ways away, so in reality, she wouldn't of minded one. But one more look at him and all of his friends, she knew she couldn't give in. Not to that.

Remembering she was going to make plans anyway, or hopefully at least, she vigorously shook her head. Sending him and his vulgar friends one last glare, she'd sneered, "fuck off, Jisung," before continuing on her way.

Back then, she didn't know how dangerous that group of boys was. She just figured they were losers who did drugs every now and then, that unfortunately, he'd turned into. She'd learned over time, that her failed attempts years ago had been wastes, it'd only led to her reputation being trashed, leading her to where she was now.

So she couldn't let herself, by any means, ever get involved with him. Not again, not ever. For she made that mistake once, and now that he was who he was now, a completely changed person for the worst, she knew she could never even think about risking it. Park Jisung was a fucking monster. She hated him with every limb in her body, and nothing could ever change that.

If only she'd known just how dangerous he'd actually became, as the echo of his dark chuckle had filled her ears despite her already being feet away from his car that still sat against the curb. "You really think you're cute, don't you?"

His intimidating words seemed to stay in the air even as the screech of the tires was heard against the street, and she'd only glanced up at the vehicle that sped past her at what felt like mock speed. Anyone other than her would probably be afraid from hearing such things, but she was used to Jisung being such a way. It was just how he was now. Every now and then, or more like every day at this point, he tried to get at her - whether it was by doing something to spite her or trying to playfully get on her good side. Truthfully, she didn't know what he expected was going to suddenly happen. Never would she suddenly turn around and be okay with him, she couldn't forgive him for that.

Curiously, her green eyes had looked up last second to watch the jet black  Audi speed away in the distance. She could still see his smirking expression in her mind then, with his lip piercing that he'd pull in between his teeth every so often - knowing it bothered her - and his covered tattoos that peeked out from the sleeves of his top. That daring expression he'd gave her when she'd glanced back to him after walking away was one she hadn't quite seen from him before. Did he finally get the message? Surely, he wasn't that dumb. He should understand by now.

Shaking the thoughts out of her head, she'd focused back on her phone. Her decision was most definitely made at this point, she was calling Si Cheng. There was nothing she needed more than to just sit down with her only friend and boast about how disgusting Park Jisung is.

Putting the iPhone to her ear, the ringing echoed through her ears as she took a deep breathe. Please don't be busy today, she hopefully thought, diverting her eyes to the still darkening sky as she walked. I need someone to talk to on a day like this.

Just when it was on the last ring and her heart began to drop, a sudden voice was heard on the opposite line.

"Hello?"

And just like that, her mood was lifted as if the nuisance of Jisung had never bothered her in the first place. Hearing the voice of someone she had trusted dearly for so long that hadn't betrayed her made her feel all that much better.

"Chengie~!" her voice was that of a child as she'd called to him in excitement, her converse clicking against the pavement which she walked on, she didn't wait to pose the question, "are you busy?"

The silence on the other line was longer than she'd hoped. In fact, he was quiet for so long she was just waiting for him to turn her down like every other time.

At this realization, she was about to speak up and say it wasn't a big deal if he was, when the sound of Si Cheng clearing his throat was heard. "Hm, no, not today."

Her green eyes brightening, she swore there was nothing that could ruin her mood at that point. Not even the rain drops she felt begin to splatter against her skin, after all, she loved rain. Jumping a bit as she walked, she'd practically squealed, "does that mean we can hang out?!"

From her obvious childish attitude, Si Cheng found himself laughing. His giggle was still to that day, completely adorable, and it caused her to smile as she waited for his reply.

"Hang out? Sure, I'll be at your place in ten?" his tone was so casual. It was as if this was any other ordinary day, as if the two of them had never grown apart in the first place. Hearing Cheng speak so normally to her like nothing had ever changed caused her heart to ache a bit, a part of her wished that nothing had.

How unfortunate those chain of events had been all those years ago.

Though thinking about how the past was no longer the present made her sad, she still pushed it to the back of her mind, finding a way to joke around, "wait, how do you know my parents aren't home?"

There was that laugh again, "like they ever are."

"Fuck, you got me."

"Okay~, I'll see you then, Hyeyeon," his heavenly voice had called sweetly to her, using her full name like he usually did. He'd always done that, and when you asked why, he'd just shrug and hum, I like it better.

The line went dead after that, and she'd found herself growing so distracted by hearing her old friend's voice again that she'd paid no attention to the fact the rain was getting heavier by the second. For it'd started out as a mere drizzle, but was now evolving into legitimate, heavy droplets that began to soak her clothes and hair.

"you're joking," she'd cursed to herself, hurriedly shoving her phone in the pocket of her romper. Holding on to the strap of her bag, she broke into a run, trying to make it home so she could get out of the rain. It was truthful she loved rain, but not when it soaked her from head to toe.

Despite the fact she was most likely going to be soaked either way since she was still far from her house, she found herself not that mad about it. At least she can finally see Cheng again.

What felt like a century later (when in reality it was only about ten minutes) she was walking up the street she lived on. The rain was even heavier at this point, the sound of it hitting the ground she walked upon making a loud splish as she squinted to see where she was even going. How long has it been? She wondered, unable to check her phone due to the pouring weather, maybe he's here by now.

Her question was soon answered as she grew closer to her home. Looking up through the droplets, she saw nothing other than that familiar red Sedan he'd always drove, ever since sophomore year. It brought back sweet yet bitter memories, to think how long it'd been since she'd even seen it, but the sight only made her eager to get home.

Breaking into a jog, she kept her head down to avoid the rain from getting on her face too much. Walking across the yard of her house, she'd found herself feeling like a wet dog when she was finally standing on the porch of the place she lived.

"Surprise!" the remembrance of the fact her friend was here seemed to slap her in the face. She hadn't jumped that time, but had simply widened her eyes as she looked up to meet the eyes of the boy she'd missed.

Her heart jumping out of her chest, she was about to jump forward out of pure excitement and hug him - but that was before she clearly looked at him. Previously, years ago, her memory of Si Cheng had consisted him being an innocent, dark haired, bright and child like boy. Thinking back to him all those years ago, before he had to move, Cheng used to hate people who dressed exactly how he was in the present. The best friend she once knew looked - on the outside - like a completely new person, and she wasn't sure how to react. Instead, she found herself frozen on the spot, her mouth slightly agape as she was gawking at him like some sort of mental patient.

Hyeyeon wasn't even sure what it was. Perhaps it was the fact his once chocolate hair was bleached into a sand-blonde, along with the fact he had real tattoos. There was one on his collarbone that her green eyes found particularly interesting, more than the ones that lined his left arm or led down to what she presumed his chest. The tattoo was rather small on his collarbone, but it was two hands making some sort of symbol she'd never seen before. She found herself staring at it longer than she'd planned, only to realize there was a number engraved on by it too - 127.

I wonder what the hell that means, she found herself thinking. His new profound appearance reminded her much of when he had turned around, betraying her, and ended up looking much like this only months later. Why had he done it? Well, because he joined a gang - but surely not.

"Hello, Hyeyeon?" she'd almost been startled for the third time today from him snapping her out of her daze. She was unsure of how long she had actually been staring at him at that point.

"Chengie~," her voice felt uneasy as she forced a smile on her face. Cheng wouldn't join anything like that, not unless he had a good reason, she had to tell herself, taking dull note of the reeking smoke that entered her nostrils.

It was clear that after all this time, he still knew her as well as he did then. "What is it? Do you dislike my new look?" he'd frowned a bit, his once bright voice fading, "Aw~, it's the earrings, isn't it?!" she could only watch in disbelief as he pouted, raising one of his hands to mess with the multiple dangling earrings from his ear.

He still acted like the child he always had been. How could he ever participate in anything like that?

Either way, she wouldn't let that tear her away from him. She knew Si Cheng well enough to know he would never do anything bad to the people he loved, and she trusted him. After knowing someone what felt like all your life, how could you not?

"No, you idiot, you look great," she'd waved a hand in dismissal. Her words of encouragement caused his dark eyes to shine once again, and there was no time until he was grinning like a kid again.

"Really? I got scared you were disgusted by me for a second," she was about to shake her head no and reassure him that could never happen - that was, until he stepped forward, opening his arms and engulfing her in a huge hug.

With wide eyes, she didn't know how to react at first. The rain still pouring from the angry sky, it wasn't long until she found herself relaxing into his arms. After all, this was her best friend Cheng she was talking about. No matter what he looked like or did, he'd always still be an angel in her eyes, and that was a fact she couldn't deny as her small arms found their way around his waist, hugging his tall figure right back.

"I missed you," his voice sounded a mere whisper, especially over the pounding of the rain against the pavement.

She couldn't help but grin to herself through out that hug from his words. Pulling away at last, she realized it'd probably be wise for the two of them to go inside, beginning to fiddle with her bag that held the house keys.

All the while doing this, she'd hummed in reply to his heartfelt confession, "then stop being so busy every time I call you." Her words dripped of sarcasm, to which Cheng wasn't very impressed with.

He watched as she dug through her bag that hung loosely off one shoulder, finally finding her keys. Hyeyeon was already unlocking the door to her house when he'd spoken again, "I'm sorry it's been so long, there's just a lot going on with me now, growing up is stressful," she couldn't help but chuckle at the pouty way he'd said such a thing.

The two of them entered the house, and as they walked inside the save atmosphere away from the hell that the weather was outside, Cheng had added, "also, I was kind of afraid of what you'd think when you saw me now," he'd motioned to himself, and she immediately had a pretty good sense of what he meant. It was obvious he was regarding the few tattoos he had spreading his skin, the two lip studs on either side of his lips, and his sandy blonde hair.

Turning on the lights in the living room which they stood in after closing the door, she'd found herself staring at him all over again. It really was different, and seeing her best friend sport such a new look after having not seen him after all those years was no doubt astonishing to her. Though it was true, the sudden change did seem suspicious in a way, but it didn't necessarily mean Si Cheng was involved in anything negative, right?

"Well," she'd cleared her throat, diverting her eyes to meet his once again, "I think you look good," she'd helplessly shrugged. Debating on if it'd be a good idea to pop the question or not, she couldn't help herself, "but why'd you do it?"

Cheng was stunned by her sudden question even though he knew it'd be coming anyway. He'd turned on his heel, walking across the wooden floor to fall onto one of the couches. Following his lead, she fell onto the sofa beside him, awaiting the answer the desperately anticipated.

"It's kind of a long story really," he'd hummed casually, leaning back into the couch and staring at the ceiling, "the school I moved to is a lot word than DMHS - violence wise. I had to fit in to keep myself safe if that makes sense. I didn't even want tattoos in the beginning, but a buddy of mine convinced me they were worth it - and not gonna lie, I think I pull them off pretty well."

She wasn't the smartest, but it was also the infinite amount of trust she had in him that made her believe him. Not noticing the fact his story was rather ridiculous, she'd only nodded in understanding, "oh, well I guess that makes sense. Your tattoos do look good, I'm just not used to seeing you look so different."

Cheng had sat up to look at her, and out of curiosity, she'd raised her hand to touch the tattoo on his arm. It was some sort of design of a skeleton trapped in a bunch of thorns, which honestly sounded idiotic - but the design was fascinating. Distracted, she ran her fingers up the design, tracing each and every strand of thorns. All the while, her old friend watched her with a humorous grin on his lips.

If only he'd told her the truth, but it wasn't worth it. The more she didn't know, the better.

Out of worry she was going to continue to ask questions about the way his life was now, Cheng had broke the silence in the room, "what about you? Jisung's not still bothering you, is he?"

Not expecting the second question, hearing his name fall off Cheng's lips caused her to look up at him. The way her eyes widened a bit after hearing it seemed to tell him enough, though. He rose a brow in question, "I'll take that as a yes?"

A long sigh left her lips, and just having to think about the disgust that Jisung was dulled her mood. She would've told him about how that boy still bothered her daily eventually, but it wasn't the first thing she'd wished to talk about after not seeing her best friend after so long.

"I don't even see him as the same person anymore," she let out a bitter chuckle, looking down to her hand that now lay in her lap. The sound of the continuous rain outside was heard as it hit the roof of the house, and soon, thunder crashing as it yelled from the sky. It was a sound she found perfectly resembling her endless anger towards Park Jisung as she went on, "he practically does whatever to annoy me every day. It's bad enough because of how everyone sees me thanks to him, but he still tries to make my life worse."

Cheng's expression had went from looking like that of a soft baby to someone ready to slaughter anyone in his path. It was true, he'd known him just like she had bad in the old days. He'd saw it all, too.

"Are you serious?" he was flaming as he thought about it, she didn't deserve that, "all you ever tried to do was help him."

"Yeah, and I regret it more every day," she scoffed, shaking her head as she played with her fingers in her lap, "clearly, there's nothing that can help him."

The thought of what Jisung was doing angered Cheng more than words could explain. To think he once saw him as a close friend. How could anyone do something like that? It was unthinkable, you don't say you love someone and then turn around and pull those sorts of things.

Perhaps Jisung thought he had it all now, but him and his friends would find out they were in for more than they could handle. And Si Cheng was going to make damn sure of that.


Chapter two; new acquaintances

Another day almost down, were the four words you'd find her repeating to herself almost three hundred times a day. These four words were practically the only thing that kept her still standing, as her feet moved one in front of the other down the halls of DMHS.

That day, in particular, had been longer than what felt like any other day, and she wasn't even sure why. Perhaps it was because she kept getting lost in her own thoughts, thinking about how her and Cheng were finally friends again after those years. Or maybe it was because she kept dreading her Statistics homework. But most likely, it was because Jisung or any of his dogs hadn't bothered her that day. Obviously, she was glad for this, but it also made her weary.

Ever since it'd all happened, Jisung had clearly grown almost - guilty for what he'd put her through. Him being the way he was now, instead of just apologizing like any other sane human being, he proceeded to attempt to do it another way. But in her eyes, she only saw it as endless annoying her until she wanted to end it all.

She'd found herself almost being able to grin that day as she plugged her earbuds into her ears, scrolling through her Spotify playlist until she found her favorite song. The melody of her favorite Muse song filled her ears, and she'd carelessly closed her eyes as she sat in the lunch room of her high school. Like every other day, she sat alone at her own table, not even eating but only slightly head-bopping to the tune that played in her ears.

The only thing that caused her to open her eyes on what felt like actually a peaceful day, was when her phone had vibrated in her hands. Her eyes opened to glance down at the lit up screen, and her heart seemed to jump a bit at the sight of a text message.

Chengie:
tell me if Jisung
bothers you

Chengie:
I'll actually go to DMHS
rn to personally beat the
shit out of him

A chuckle left her lips as she read it. How glad she was to be friends with Si Cheng again after having not spoken to him in what felt like centuries.

Hyeyeon~:
he actually hasn't
bothered me today

Hyeyeon~:
yet

Hyeyeon~:
I might be speaking
too soon tbh

She figured that sometime throughout the rest of the day, Jisung would attempt sticking his head up her ass again just like every other day. As it was something she'd grown so used to, her days hadn't been normal in forever.

Even then, it wasn't like it was qualified as normal. She still got dirty looks from students as she passed, and the occasional hey, can you get me some drugs, too? comment. In reality, her life couldn't be classified as normal, but this was as close as she'd get to it.

To her surprise, the rest of the day went by smoothly. It wasn't long until she was heading into her last period, otherwise known as English 4. It would've been her favorite class because she loved English, too bad the teacher was such an idiot.

Either way, she continued to hum the Muse song she was listening to at that point as her feet made their way to sit in her usual seat. It was at the very back of the room in the corner, a special place she liked to sit at in every class. And like every other class, no one dared to sit beside her.

It wasn't like she cared, though. All she cared about was texting Cheng, which is what you'd find her doing while she waited for the bell to ring, indicating the class was starting. The teacher wasn't even in the room yet, (thank god, because if she was she'd already be running her mouth.) The class was rather empty as she was one of the first people in it. However, the few students that where didn't fail to look at her with gross looks on their faces.

In that moment, she was snapped out of the idiotic conversation she'd been having with her close friend by the sound of the bell screeching in her ear. She'd been giggling to herself as she clicked on the photo Cheng had sent of himself. Fucking christ, she shook her head in disbelief, finding herself growling lost whilst staring at the photo of her friend.

The feeling she felt in the pit of her stomach was one she ignored just like every time she spoke to him since they'd become friends again. Or perhaps it was that she hadn't even noticed it yet in the first place.

Realizing class was starting, she'd put her phone on mute after telling Cheng that he was only slightly intimidating just so he'd shut up (and also turning off her music), slipping it into the bag that hung off the back of her chair. Shifting to make herself comfortable, she felt - content that day. Her green eyes watched the perfect view she had of the outside world from her seat at the back corner, right by the rows of windows that lined the left side of the room.

Like every other day, she could feel stares directed at her. The sound of the teacher entering the room was heard, and she braced herself for the endless bullshit she was most likely going to hear about the drama she'd watched on Lifetime last night. I wish I was joking, she thought bitterly, facing the front to watch the last few students enter the classroom.

Expecting the teacher to start going on about whatever it was she was going to waste time with that day, she didn't. Instead, the old woman that taught English 4 had looked to the door, along with everyone else. Curiously, the girl who sat alone in the back found herself looking as well.

At first, she grew confused, as her slow working brain tried to process who she was looking at. I've never seen this guy before, who the hell is he? His caramel hair was parted in the middle, his seemingly simple colored brown eyes glistening from the beaming lights. He was wearing all black, his jeans distressed and ripped, with his backpack hanging loosely off one shoulder. To top it all off, he even had dangling earrings.

Her brows furrowed as she watched him stand by the teachers desk, politely grinning at her. His smile seemed to brighten the entire room itself, and right then, he seemed like the sun himself, awaiting for her to assign him a seat.

The old woman at the front of the room behind the desk almost seem mesmerized herself as she returned the grin. "Sit wherever you want," she waved a hand dismissively, knowing that was what he wanted. He'd only kindly nodded, before looking towards the class. His brown eyes slowly raked over the entire room, that seemed practically full with no empty spots whatsoever, that was until you got to her.

While he was still standing up there, Ms. Evans had motioned to the young boy, "class, be kind towards your new classmate, Jaemin."

A few students had mumbled some lame shit in reply she wasn't paying attention to. She could only watch as his eyes had landed on all the empty seats, all located around her. Someone's probably already told him about it, she figured, waiting for the angel-like boy to give her some sort of dirty look since the school never failed to spread bullshit like wildfires.

But he hadn't, he'd only grinned as he made eye contact with her from across the room.


He caught me staring, she winced from her own idiocy, quickly breaking the eye contact and looking down to her desk. Has he not heard yet? She tried not to look back up at where he was going despite her growing curiosity. It was when she heard growing footsteps in her direction that she had a bad feeling, her breathe almost hitched in her throat as she realized where he was going to sit.

Don't sit by me, her mind pleaded as if the boy could hear her somehow, they'll all tell you soon enough. The last thing she wanted was to socialize and have a chance at meeting a new friend, only for them to turn around and betray her. This was why she refused to trust anyone, and she wasn't going to start then.

The sound of his bag being dropped onto the floor purposely was heard. And her green eyes dared to look up, only to see him casually slipping into the seat beside her.

Her brain felt the incredible urge to explode, and she could feel him looking at her once again, and no doubt everyone in the room. Don't make eye contact, she told herself harshly, instead actually listening for once as the teacher went on her idiotic rant for the day.

The day that had felt so quickly paced seemed to pass extremely slow that last class period. She didn't know if it was because of how much she was anticipating hopefully getting home without being bothered by the mistake of her past, or if it was because of the new student that had her feeling shaken up for just sitting beside her. Guess that's how much she dislikes people - except for Cheng.

Whatever it was, it felt like the class period lasted the length of the entire day itself. Is it ever going to end? She dreaded every single thing that was happening, she swore she could feel his brown eyes continuously glancing over to her.

The pencil felt fragile in her tiny hand that seemed to almost be shaking as she tried to take the notes for that day. I'm used to stares, so why am I reacting this way?

"You'll need all the notes from the last week for the quiz tomorrow," Ms. Evans had been saying as she finished scribbling one last thing on the whiteboard, "if you don't have them, ask a classmate. If they don't let you use them, tough luck."

Please tell me the class is ending. As if on queue with her pained thoughts, the bell had signaled a high-pitched scream. Without noticing, a huge breathe of relief had left her lips as she'd shot to her feet.

Forcing herself not to look at anyone else in the room, she began to pack up her things. Closing her notebook now that she had all the notes for the quiz she definitely was not gonna study for, she'd raised it, about to slip it into her bag as the last thing she needed to put away. That was, until she heard someone clear their throat beside her.

She tried not to show what she really felt, instead making her face blank as she looked to where it'd come from. Maybe it's not even towards me, but her gut was telling her otherwise.

However, when she'd looked to the desk that was beside hers, she'd saw the new student which she'd thought had been trying to get her attention, completely involved with nothing more than a group of girls. The sight she hadn't wanted to witness caused her to wince. He's not even that cute, she could only shake her head as she watched the girls practically melting as they stood before his tall figure.

"Since you don't have the notes, you can totally use mine," one of the girls she never cared to know of had grinned up at him. Frankly, her fake attempt at a cute smile made her look that of a cow instead, along with the fact her outfit was three sizes too small for her.

The other girls had offered the same thing, something to do with the notes. In the end, the boy - Jaemin - hadn't seemed very interested at all. Meanwhile, the girls were getting upset with each other over the fact they all wanted him to only use their notes. Jaemin had stood as they began to fight with each other, complaining about how they'd 'called him first.'

He seemed almost disgusted as he watched them, before he'd coughed a bit to get their attention. "Um, that's really nice of you guys, but I'm not an object to call dibs on - and uh, she already offered to let me use hers," she'd still been watching him address the girls when he'd unexpectedly turned to point at her. At the realization she was now being looked at, and had been caught watching, she almost had a heart attack on the spot.

With wide eyes, she was unsure of what the fuck he was doing at first. It was when she met his brown eyes with her shocked green ones, he gave her a pleading expression. Oh, he wants to get them away - no shit.

"Right!" her voice had sounded fake, and cracked a bit as she held her notebook in the air awkwardly. Quickly clearing her throat, she returned to her normal state, "I'm letting him use my notes."

The three girls had sent her looks of both fear and disgust. "You're borrowing them from her?" one of them had gasped in disbelief.

Here it comes, she presumed, and just like that, "watch out, don't let her drug you," the overweight one had sneered, wrinkling her nose when she met Hyeyeon's eyes.

There were two options she had in such a moment, and like always, she took option B. "You should watch yourself, or you'll be next," as she said these words with venom, she was actually laughing inside.

Either way, the girls had looked at her like she was some sort of absolute evil. "Let's get out of here, it doesn't matter," one of them had whispered, and the other two had vigorously nodded in agreement. Watching as they ran out of the room like they were being chased by something supernatural, she couldn't help but snicker.

Distracted in thought for a moment, she completely forgot about what that entire situation had been about in the first place. It was when the sound of the new student's voice broke her out of her thoughts that she'd finally been slapped back into reality, "I don't think I can thank you enough for that."

His eyes were kind as she met them. The way he presented himself made him seem almost soft but also like someone you most likely wouldn't want to be on bad terms with. It was something she hadn't seen in a guy before. I hope he's not involved in the bad side of this place, she found herself thinking in worry as she disobeyed all of the things she'd swore to herself about not making any new friends nor acquaintances period, returning the smile he'd sent her earlier.

"Sure, I know what they were really trying to get at, and I don't think anyone would want to poke that with a stick," he'd chuckled at her comment before there was a moment of silence, before she realized she was still holding the notebook in her hand. Walking a bit forward to stand before him, he towered over her almost as much as Cheng did, meaning she had to look up at him as she offered, "the notes?" holding out the book to him.

She was never this nice to anyone, excluding Cheng. This was some serious special treatment this person was receiving, and to think she didn't even know him.

He'd only waved a hand of dismissal in the air, "it's okay, I don't actually even need the notes. They kind of just berated me the second the bell rang."

Her hand that had held the notebook fell back to her side, but she wasn't actually offended, or was she? "Ah," she'd hummed slowly, "if you say so."

Jaemin had watched her facial expressions carefully. He seemed to read everything on her face, and had quickly spoken up, feeling like he might've offended her. In reality, it was just that he already knew all of the content for the quiz so he most likely wouldn't need to study.

"Actually, I should probably study," she'd seemed surprised from his sudden change of mind. Before she knew it, he was reaching out a hand for the notebook.

"Oh - okay," feeling confused, she placed it in his extended hand without a second thought.

There was that sweet smile again, he'd slipped it into his bag that was set on the chair of his desk, "thanks for the help."

She only shrugged, already grabbing her bag and throwing it over her shoulder after getting her phone out of it. "It's no problem."

After this was said, she was sure there was no conversation left. Figuring that was that, she was just about to make her way out of the room when he'd stopped her by speaking again.

"Hey," she'd slowly paused in her movements, only having taken one step towards the exit, "by the way, I'm Jaemin, Na Jaemin."

Na Jaemin, the name seemed to repeat in his head. Unsure of what to say, she only nodded, I guess this is the part where I introduce myself, apparently. Having not expected the sudden introduction, she sent him a close-lipped smile, "Hyeyeon."

He couldn't help but stare for a moment. Why do I feel like I've heard that name somewhere?

"Nice to meet you, Hyeyeon. I don't know what those girls were talking about, by the way, but you seem pretty cool."

Her face remained blank as she stared at him. Pursing her lips, she'd replied, "thanks, Jaemin, I'll see you tomorrow."

And with that, she left. But Na Jaemin still found his way onto her mind the entire way home, all the while, there was no sign of Park Jisung.

She chuckled as she thought of the conversation they had had only this morning, staring down at her phone as she expected him to reply with in seconds like always. It was when minutes passed that turned into hours, she found herself pouting as she had been doing homework now that night. Checking her phone, there was still no reply.

Why is he ignoring me so suddenly? She internally groaned as she powered her phone off again. Cheng was literally the only person she had to talk to. Even her parents weren't home since they were always gone for business overseas, leaving her to fend alone. This wasn't exactly difficult or anything since she was at the age of 17 and could function normally as a human, but fuck, all she wanted was someone to talk to.

Sighing in frustration, she rose to her feet, deciding to shower all her worries away. Grabbing all of the important essentials, she skipped her way into the restroom connected to her bedroom. Humming to herself, she prepared to shower, and was perfectly ready after turning on Muse to match with the mood she was currently feeling.

The next thirty minutes you'd find her showering in deep thought while still managing to attempt the high note in Showbiz. "Jaemin! I didn't know you were moving today," the old friend on the other line had spoke brightly to him as he'd leaned against the brick wall of his new high school. He felt rather annoyed that the person that had promised to pick him up hadn't showed up the entire day, being that he was also a student at the school.

He hadn't actually heard his actual voice in a long time. For sure, he sounded a lot different than he'd expected. They definitely weren't kids anymore, that was a proven fact. The only time he'd really ever spoken to him had been over text.

"Uh, yeah, I kind of told you that," he heaved out a sigh at how forgetful his friend was - or maybe it was that he just didn't care.

The boy on the other line had noticed his tone of annoyance greatly, "hey, hey, I'm sorry, ight? If you need a ride, I can come pick you up right now, but a few of my friends might come along if you don't mind." Jaemin winced as he heard the other voice on the line, did he just fucking say 'ight' like that?

His house wasn't even that far he thought, but being as unsure as he was, he didn't feel like finding out for it to only be miles away. So what felt like his only option was agreeing as he hummed carelessly, "alright, whatever."

"Nice, see you in a bit then, Jae-Jae," the child hood nickname made him want to reach through the phone and personally hit him, but he'd only called a okay in reply, before the line abruptly went dead.

A sigh left his lips as he stared ahead, slipping his phone in the back pocket of his skinny jeans. Most people were gone from the school by now, leaving it practically deserted. I wonder what part of town she lives in, he found himself curiously thinking of the girl he'd met, maybe it's the same way as mine.

Not having any earbuds to listen to music, he found himself just humming whatever song came into his head first instead. He found himself getting lost in thinking about many random things that crossed his mind suddenly. One of them ended up being her all over again, but it was a question he couldn't help but be curious about. She was so nice, so why did everyone seem to dislike her so much? Those girls had mentioned something about her trying to drug him? It sounded fucking insane, there was no way a girl like that would try to do something like that.

Shaking his head in disbelief, he wondered what Hyeyeon had really done to have the entire school against her. His friend ended up taking longer than he expected, so he'd groaned as he sat down on the pavement, setting his bag beside him.

Without thinking, he'd pulled out that notebook. It was a rather fancy notebook for just being for English 4, with her name neatly printed on the first page. Jaemin's brows creased downward in concentration as he flipped through the pages, seeing not only boring notes - but cute doodles she liked to do on each page, most likely when she got bored (and she sure did from how often Ms. Evans runs her mouth.)

After flipping for what felt like years, he'd run across the notes that were needed for the quiz. He'd began to read them when he found her doodles more interesting instead. The way she drew things like animals and cute cartoons had him chuckling to himself.

Before he could even process his own actions, he found himself digging inside his bag for a pencil. Pulling it out, he rose his hand swiftly before he began to draw a doodle of his own in the corner of a new page after today's notes. Jaemin wasn't even talented in drawing, but seeing her's seemed to give him some sort of inspiration.

It took him a bit, but after erasing certain parts and redrawing them multiple times - only to have messed up again - he finally finished a doodle of his own. He'd drew something he at least saw rather original, nothing other than his favorite Kakao Friends character, Ryan. In his drawing, Ryan was laying on his side, holding himself up on his arms with a rose in his mouth.

When he'd finished the masterpiece, he stopped his drawing movements to just admire his creation. Satisfied, he quickly scribbled a NJM atop the drawing, even adding a little heart next to it, just so she knew who it was from.

Having had been so involved in his own silly doings, he'd was startled by the sound of someone suddenly calling his name. As if this wasn't enough, the sharp honk of a vehicle was heard as it pulled up by the curb, only feet away from where he sat on the pavement in front of the school.

Jaemin's eyes had whipped up from the notebook to see his friend rolling down the window, and his eyes widened at the sight. How the hell does the have a brand new Audi? His mind was boggled, unable to process what he was even witnessing.

The next thing that astonished him was the fact there were what looked like three - maybe four - other guys in the vehicle with him. And from where he was sitting, who he once knew as his old friend looked like a completely different person - to match how he sounded on the phone.

"Jaemin, hurry the fuck up, dude!" Jisung had called from the drivers seat of the jet black car.

Snapping himself out of his shock, Jaemin rose to his feet, casually packing the notebook and pencil back into his bag. Throwing it over his shoulder, he wearily made his way to the car that was waiting for him. Seeing the passenger seat was open, he swung open the door, ducking to get inside.

He wasn't even settled in the car when Jisung began to parade him. "Yo~, Na Jaemin, long time no see!" he reached over to pat him on the shoulder.

Jaemin could only stare at him - what the hell seemed to be the only words he could think. When he'd assumed Jisung looked like a new person, this wasn't what he meant. He didn't expect to climb into the car only to see he was completely unrecognizable. With his bleached hair, multiple ear piercings, and tattooed body - he had no idea who he was.

Jisung seemed to notice him staring and cheekily grinned, "I look dope, right?"

He tried not to cringe from his awful vocabulary and the reeking smell of smoke. "Different, that's for sure," was all he said, causing Jisung to only laugh in reply, slamming his foot on the pedal without warning. It'd caused the car to jerk forward, almost sending him flying from the speed he carelessly drove at. Suddenly, Jaemin felt himself regretting his decision.

"Oh - right - meet my buddies, by the way," Jisung had motioned to the back, where Jaemin hadn't gotten a chance to look due to how distracted he'd been by the sight of his old friend.

Reluctantly, his brown eyes fell on the three boys that sat, and he completely understood where the endless smell of smoke had been coming from. A cigarette hung loosely out of one of their mouths, and he tried not to seem awkward as he took in all of their appearances.

All four of them had something in common which was for sure - infinite fucking tats - with an occasional piercing here and there. That was what he thought until he laid eyes on the last boy who sat directly behind him on the far left. He doesn't look like he belongs here, he noted, realizing the poor guy looked like he'd been kidnapped from middle school.

The one in the middle spoke up suddenly, clearing his throat, "nice to meet you, Jaemin, I'm Jeno," he'd offered the smallest of smiles before he'd stuck his cigarette in his mouth again after exhaling the smoke. After removing it from his lips once again, he motioned to the side where the kidnapped-looking boy sat, "and this is Chenle. We know he looks a little off."

Chenle had looked to Jaemin from his eyes having previously been focused on the window. Pushing his circular framed glasses up his nose, he offered him a genuine looking, kind smile, "It's on purpose, really. I'm also just smarter than these dimwits."


Jaemin only knew to nod in understanding, watching as Jeno had glared at the boy from his comment. "Are you trying to get shot or something?" the boy who had introduced himself first asked the one beside him. He couldn't help but wonder just why Chenle's appearance was apparently 'on purpose,' though. Compared to the others, to say he looked weird was a crazy understatement.

Chenle had rolled his eyes, "oh please, do you actually have a gun on you right now-" He was cut off when Jeno had shifted in his seat, his hand reaching in his pocket to pull out nothing other than a fucking weapon. Jaemin wasn't educated enough to know what kind of gun it was, but either way it had him startled as he grew tense in his seat. However, everyone else in the vehicle seemed unimpressed. Chenle had only sighed in seeming disappointment, shaking his head as he looked back out the window, "I stand corrected."

Through out this, there was still one last boy that hadn't introduced himself. Curiously, he'd looked to him, only to see he'd been lost in texting on his phone the entire time. Shiny, long earrings dangled from only one of his ears, and his dark brown hair was perfectly parted on either sides of his head.

He must've caught Jaemin's stares, because he suddenly looked up, noticing he was looking. "Oh," he hummed, realizing his mistake, "sup, I'm Renjun. Sorry if that seemed rude, I'm just finishing up a last few orders."

A last few orders - of what? He wanted to ask, but was almost worried to. He was finding out too much about them too fucking fast. Firstly, this guy dressed like a Harry Potter look a like on purpose for some reason. Then, this guy casually carries around a weapon in his pocket and carelessly whips it the fuck out. And now, this guy runs some sort of - business?

To think he'd only been in Chicago for a few days - he didn't know what to think. Jaemin had no idea of the things that went on in such a city, a city he'd soon learn was full of dark things he never planned to witness in the first place. If only he knew then what he'd be forced into, and just how different his old friend really was.

The car was silent only minutes later after he'd input his address in the GPS. On the radio, some rap song he didn't know the name of blasted at almost full volume since Jisung had cranked it up. Being that the bass input was set so high, the entire car felt like it was about to explode as they drove. Jaemin's eardrums felt like they were bleeding, it took all of his well being to contain himself with the music and the strong scent of smoke.

"So, Jae, how was your first day at DMHS?" Jisung had hummed a normal conversation unexpectedly.

Jaemin had to think about such a question for a minute. To be truthful, nothing had happened at all, just a lot of annoying girls he didn't want anything to do with and idiotic guys thinking they were cool with the things they said to him. He ended up thinking rather hard about anything he could tell his friend that would even be slightly interesting, but his mind was almost blank.

"Uh, nothing really happened," he had finally shrugged.

Unsatisfied with his reply, Jisung slapped his arm, driving with one hand, "come on, seriously, you didn't meet any hot girls or anything?!"

Pursing his lips, he tried to think of anything to say. Honestly, he could've just lied, but in the end he'd casually spoke, "well, I met this girl, actually, but I don't think I'd categorize her as-," he'd been cut off by his friend's weirdly excited voice.

"Nice, man, what's her name?"

Maybe you'd know if you wouldn't of fucking cut me off. He cleared his throat, blocking his bitter thoughts out, "Hyeyeon."

He'd watched as Jisung's face turned one of surprise. He looked like he'd just seen some sort of horrific scene right in front of his eyes, and Jaemin furrowed his brows as he watched him seem to be in some sort of serious debate with himself.

At the sound of such a name, the three boys in the back had tuned into the conversation as well, their eyes filled with curiosity.

"Really - you talked to her?" he said this like it was some sort of sin to have spoken to her, it only caused him to grow more confused, "did she tell you anything about herself?"

Interesting question to ask. "No, not really, I just met her today last period. Why, do you know anything about her?"

Almost instant, Jisung was shaking his head, "hm, no, not really, but I hear she's pretty fucked in the head."


Chapter four; nicknames

Si Cheng's brows creased downward in concentration, but also confusion, as he'd read Hyeyeon's texts. He scrolled back up on the conversation to re-read the name of the guy she said she'd met, repeating it in his head multiple times. Cheng knew he should be well aware of the people his age that were involved in the same things as himself - but that was just the thing. What if he wasn't from this part of Chicago, but a different part? There was also the chance, that 'Na Jaemin' wasn't actually bad at all like Hyeyeon was insisting, but that didn't mean he wasn't going to make sure.

Forgetting to even reply to the poor girl's texts, he'd slipped his phone in his back pocket. His feet were quick ahead of him as he made up the stairs of the porch to the house. Cheng practically lived here at this point, as his relationship with his parents were rusty and unstable - plus, since he was 18, they couldn't keep him at his own will anymore. This added to the reason he saw these people as family, and he'd do whatever to protect them.

The sun beaming down on his back from the sky, he'd dug his house key out of his bag. Shoving it into the key hole, the commotion wasn't anything new to his ears as he made his way inside. The loud, heavy music that always played boomed from the loud speakers that hung off the walls in the corner of the main room. Cheng threw his bag aside as he entered it, the smell of marijuana filling his nostrils almost instantly.

At the sound of his bag hitting the wood floor, the three friends that were lounging on the couches spread around the room had looked up from getting completely stoned. Si Cheng's eyes raked over the three, noticing the person he actually wanted to talk to was missing.

"Hey, my man Win-Win!" Johnny had rose to his feet to give him a side hug, the others soon following with their own greetings, using what they called his 'gang name.'

There was a blunt loosely hanging from Jaehyun's lips as he watched Cheng's stressed expression as the boy had sat next to the other three. "you look like you need a pick up, dude," he'd noted the boy's almost miserable looking demeanor.

Brushing his blonde hair out of his face, Cheng shook his head at the blunt Jaehyung was offering him, "I'm fine, where's Taeyong?" He got right to the point, in desperate search for their leader so he could attempt to get the information he was searching for.

They'd all exchanged looks, before Doyoung had cleared his throat. Pushing his glasses up his nose, he informed casually, "in his office probably dealing with important things, so I wouldn't recommend bothering him." He would've chuckled at Doyoung's fake glasses any other day, but right then, he was in too deep of thought to make fun of his friend. It's a fashion statement, WinWin, you wouldn't understand, is what he'd always say when you'd pester him about them.

He'd also noticed the other two that were missing from the group, but like everyone else, he had a clear idea of where they were and what they were doing. And it was for sure something he didn't want to think about.

"Why do you seem so eager to talk to him, what's on your mind, little buddy?" Johnny had asked, his voice barely coming out comprehensible from how stoned he was. Him and Jaehyun did this practically everyday, and even skipped school to do it. It was rather funny, as Doyoung usually hung out with them, too. But he wasn't one for marijuana.

Unsure if he should even bother bringing up the subject with him, Cheng diverted his eyes to his lap as he thought about it. They were all knowledgeable too, there was a likely chance they might know something, he found himself realizing.

Without a second thought, he posed the question, "have you guys heard of this guy named Jaemin?"

They'd all exchanged looks, causing him to think they might know who he was. However, all hope was lost when Johnny's stoned ass had rose to his feet, screaming the name, "Taemin?" And before he could even proclaim that that definitely was not who he was fucking talking about, he started to attempt the dance to Move.

You're fucking joking, was the look you'd find Cheng giving his friend. The shit Johnny did even when he wasn't stoned never failed to make him want to jump off a bridge, and to think he was childish, too.

Jaehyun had started laughing at Johnny's awful dance moves, completely ignoring the question Si Cheng had even asked. Thankfully, there was someone in the room who wasn't completely stoned and actually had brain cells. Doyoung seemed to be in deep thought as he pursed his lips.

"What's his last name?"

"Na," he'd replied in only a millisecond, desperately wanting to know if he knew anything about the mystery boy his best friend was getting involved with.

Doyoung leaned his chin in the palm of his hand as he leaned back into the sofa, his brown eyes narrowed at the ceiling in thought. "Na Jaemin..." he repeated the name, trying to think of if he'd possibly heard it anywhere to help out his seemingly desperate friend.

"I don't think I've ever heard of him," he finally hummed, "but I can sure keep an eye out anytime I'm selling."

A bit disappointed, Cheng told himself he should be happy about this. It was good he didn't end up being some sort of gang member that shot people on the daily. This meant his best friend wasn't in any danger from him, right?

"Thanks, Doyoung," he grinned gratefully, his friend only shrugging it off like nothing.

You should never speak too soon.

There was a while of silence between the two, who filled it by watching their other two friends be complete idiots. This wasn't exactly a typical day in the gang house, but it wasn't anything new, either.

A long sigh left his lips as Cheng leaned back in the sofa, closing his eyes as if to cherish the peaceful moment he was having. For once, there was no work to be done at the house and he could just sit and breathe.

At least he hoped this was the case, until the sound of heavy footsteps had been heard rushing into the room, followed by the slam of a door. The sight of the leader entering the room, looking like he was prepared to work, was further assumed once he landed eyes on the gun that rested in his hand.

Doyoung had looked at Taeyong with the same serious expression he always had, "Work?"

Brushing strands of red hair out of his face, he'd only strictly nodded. The leader's eyes had raked over the couches to see the other two stoned idiots, to which he'd only shook his head, pulling his silver lip ring in between his lips in thought.

"We were hired, it needs to be done now. I only need two people to come with me," he'd finally explained once his eyes fell on Doyoung and Si Cheng once again.

The two already knew what he was thinking as they rose to their feet. Si Cheng tried not to show how displeased he was that he was assigned for more work. Oh well, he shook his head mentally, it's better than being stuck with these two idiots.

"Get the guns, I'll wait in the car."

Those were the last texts she had sent Si Cheng yesterday. It was now a new day, Friday to be exact. She couldn't expect him to always be speaking to her, and she was used to being alone.

It was rather pointless for her to even go to the cafeteria since she never had any plans to eat in the first place, but hey, where else did she have to go? It wasn't like she had a car despite her parents wealth.

Undisclosed Desires blasted full volume through her earbuds. Any sane person would imagine it hurt to listen to music at such a high level, but the bouncing brunette didn't care as she made her way down the long hallway. She was even singing the words, probably rather loud, but it wasn't like it gained her anymore looks than she would've gotten otherwise.

It was when a sudden figure had seemed to fall from the sky that she almost tripped and had a literal heart attack on the spot. Being more engrossed in the music than she thought, she hadn't seen the familiar boy stepping out in front of her, nor heard him call her name thanks to her earbuds being at max volume.

Some sort of mixture of a squeal and scream left her lips as she tripped right over his foot. The unfortunate events that would've occurred if he hadn't of cared enough to hurriedly reach out an arm, catching her frail body from hitting smack on the floor. The once giddy smile that'd turned afraid once he realized she tripped from lack of attention returned to Jaemin's face as he helped her stand up straight.

A look of shock still evident on her face, her eyes slowly went from where they had been the entire time - on the ground - to go from the black boots he wore once again that day to the simple white t-shirt until they were at his chocolate eyes. Jaemin was staring at her, that smile of his still lingering on his lips, and she found herself getting lost in a trance once again. "Sorry for almost tripping you," he'd said as they now stood normally before each other, his tone genuine, "I was going to ask you if I could eat with you."

The blank stare of surprise she gave him seemed to throw him off guard. Jaemin was thinking the complete opposite of what it actually meant as he grew nervous under her gaze, clearing his throat, "Is that not okay? Sorry, I can ask my friend-," she cut him off in worry that he'd taken her unreadable look the wrong way.

"No!" she accidentally yelled, causing more eyes to be on the two than there already where, "uh - it's fine, we can sit together."

Jaemin found himself grinning thankfully, "Alright, well, lead the way then, Yeonnie."

She'd nodded curtly, beginning to walk with him practically beside her. It took her a moment, before she realized what he'd just called her. As they walked into the cafeteria, having had been only feet away from it when they had had the previous conversation, she looked up to him with furrowed brows, "what'd you just call me?"

He chuckled at her bewildered expression, "I just made it up, the last part of your name. I thought it was cute." It was hard not to almost melt at the sight of his sweet smile he tended to show more than often. If my smile was that gorgeous, I'd show it off, too.

There was a short moment of silence between the two. Commotion struck greatly in the cafeteria of DMHS like any other normal day, and the two friends made their way to the corner where they'd sit together. The usual lonely table that'd be filled with a singular soul now had a new one to say hello to. It was a sight that had many students mind boggled as they watched the new student Na Jaemin walk with her. The whispers that spread were obvious, and she noticed them greatly. Jaemin, on the other hand, didn't seem the slightest of bothered as he casually set his bag down beside her seat, taking his own.

Pursing her lips as she tried to ignore the looks they were getting, it seemed harder when she knew it wasn't only about her but also him. Perhaps it was because she was afraid of what kind of rumors would be spread this time, or if she could really trust Jaemin to even begin with. The last thing she needed was him being the one to start them. But surely, he wasn't that kind of person.

"Do you not like the nickname?" she hadn't expected him to ask this question, having had been in to deep of thought about the fact he'd called the name cute. Why would someone like her need a cute nickname?

Thinking about it for a second, she finally shrugged, "I like it, I've just never been called that before." What could it hurt?

Jaemin was clearly happy to hear those words, "that makes it better, it's my nickname for you." She tried to hide the smile that began to spread across her lips, instead diverting her eyes to the table they sat at. The boy beside her had rose to his feet, most likely preparing to go get his tray of food.

Expecting her to follow his lead so they could go together, when he didn't, he'd stared down at her in confusion, "aren't you gonna come get lunch?" he'd asked, as if to remind her.

Hyeyeon had looked up to meet his caring, warm eyes, slowly shaking her head, "No, I'm alright. Go ahead."

But he wasn't content with such an answer. It'd only caused him to pout as he continued to look down at her, "are you sure? I get the school food isn't that great, but it's not good to go the rest of the day without eating, Yeonnie~."

His warmhearted words hurt her insides, but she still only shook her head no, "I'm okay, really."

Although reluctant, Jaemin had nodded in understanding. However, before he went to get his tray, he'd leaned down to unzip his backpack. She'd diverted her attention from him by this time, pulling out her phone to check if Cheng had finally replied to her or not. Suddenly, a familiar purple notebook was placed onto the tan-wood table before her, snapping her attention.

"There's your English notebook by the way, I appreciate you letting me use it," Jaemin had gratefully thanked her before she could even process what was sitting before her.

She didn't even get a chance to say it was no problem, because when she looked up he was already in the lunch line. A small smile had made it's way onto her lips as she watched his buoyant movements, even the way he walked. Jaemin wasn't actually even a social type, he just was content with the world itself. He'd always smile at people and greet them, that was just him.

Her hand had rested carefully atop her notebook that he'd given back to her as she found herself accidentally getting lost in watching him all over again. He'd rock back and forth on his feet as he stood in line, grinning at anyone who spoke to him and politely most likely telling girl's he wasn't interested. She figured he wouldn't think to look at her so there wasn't anything she had to worry about.

That was, until his brown eyes had directed from someone he was talking to. They raked over the entire cafeteria, and before she knew it, were looking right at her. It was just like that day all over again, and as her heart freaked out - he'd only threw her that pretty smile he loved to show the entire world.

Chapter five; ryan


The rest of the lunch period had went around rather quickly. She hadn't paid attention to the time in the slightest, and had been surprised when the bell had suddenly let out a deafening ring. I thought it just started, she'd thought in confusion as the current conversation her and Jaemin had been having ended.

He'd rose to his feet beside her, that grin staying on his lips as she followed his actions. The two of them had been laughing with each other and making jokes the entire period. Usually, she had to act 'fake nice' to people, but with Nana, it wasn't like that. It was the first time anyone had been able to genuinely make her smile humorously in a long time that wasn't Cheng. She found herself admiring how caring he was towards her. Nana didn't pay attention to any of the looks they received, and he never once asked her just why the students hated her so much.

"I'll walk you to class," he'd hummed as they began to walk together, being the very last students to leave the cafeteria. However, they weren't the only ones who tended to take their precious time leaving. "What's your next period?"

Not noticing the eyes that burned holes into her back, Hyeyeon only hummed in reply, "Calculus."

One thing she had learned about Na Jaemin, was he loved math. It was something she could never imagine doing herself, and it almost disgusted her. How could you want to major in math? What a fucking nightmare.

"I'll lead the way, ma'dam," he playfully spoke, before picking up the pace at which he walked. She rolled her eyes, having to jog a bit to keep up with his athletic figure. He noticed her carelessly attempting this, and only sped up his pace further. At this point, he was practically running down the halls. It caused her to groan in annoyance, knowing he was doing it all on purpose.

He'd laughed as he looked at her glum expression, and she caught his gaze on her, "I'm gonna hurt you, Nana."

It wasn't long until the two of them were standing right before the Calculus class, also known as her next period. He'd been chuckling as he stood beside the door of the room, motioning to it like a chauffeur. She finally caught up to where he was standing, and gave him an unimpressed look.

Unphased, he'd only winked, "I bet you are. Have fun in calculus."

Before another empty threat could leave her lips, he was already waving and walking off to his own class. This ended up in her only shaking her head as she watched him go, eventually waving back. Na Jaemin, you're something else.

Turning her back towards the door once he'd disappeared into another room down the hall, her hand was just reaching for the handle. The entire time they'd walked to the senior classes, neither of them had had any idea of just who had been following right behind them. This was why she was confused and terrified at the sudden action of someone grabbing the wrist of the arm that wasn't about to have opened the door.

The mystery human had pulled her back, away from her calculus class that she was now late to. A squeal left her lips as she hurriedly whipped around to meet the eyes of whatever idiotic being had the audacity to pull such a thing - especially to her.

But the face which she was greeted with only caused her expression to grow aloof. Instantly, she ripped her wrist free from his arm in disgust, about to voice out her thoughts of how he was an absolute piece of garbage before turning right back and going into her class. It was when she went to do this right after freeing her wrist that she looked around her, only to see five other boys surrounding her on every possible escape route. Her throat suddenly felt dry as she processed what she was dealing with. It was all of Jisung and his fucking dogs - at least a far as she knew. Who knew how fucking many there were of them she didn't know about.

The sight of the tattooed, harsh looking boys - except for the one she knew as Chenle - wasn't that intimidating to her since she'd known them so well. A sigh left her lips instead as she faced her ex once again, "what the fuck do you want?"

Jisung chuckled at her harsh tone she always seemed to show him. She only continued to give him the blank, angered expression she always did, letting her eyes rake over his facial features all the way to his tattoos. It was almost upsetting to see him the way he was, was all she could think as the nauseating strong scent of smoke and other things she couldn't name filled her nostrils.

"I see you're well acquainted with the new kid, huh?" he'd rose a brow questioningly at her, speaking these words as she'd been staring at what she called his 'gang tattoo.' She'd noticed that him and all of his dogs had some sort of tattoo that symbolized their 'group.' It was until then she had never looked at it much.

Snapping back into reality and the fact that there were literally six gang members surrounding her, she shrugged, "not like it's your business."

However, her ex boyfriend didn't seem too phased by her usual tone towards him. Jisung had let out some sort of dramatic sigh, diverting his brown eyes towards the ceiling as if he was dreading what he was about to do. It was all clearly in act, which she knew well. He didn't give a damn about what he inflicted on the people around him, and this was shown when he took a step forward to push his body against hers that was already leaning on the cold, metal locker. That devious smirk of his spread right over his lips as he reached up to grip both of her wrists harshly, pinning them above her head.

This action caused a short gasp to leave her lips, the first instinct being to try to break free. In the end, she knew well enough his grip was far too strong compared to hers, and even then, she had a feeling it would only make her situation worse with all of his dogs around.

Fuck, she mentally cursed, refusing to look into his eyes that she despised with every ounce of blood in her body, no one is in the halls at this fucking time? It made no possible sense to her. Was it possible they made everyone stay out of the hall or something? If only she knew then what kind of power they really held.

Her head was to the side as she wouldn't meet his eyes. This tended to anger Jisung as he'd continued to hold her wrists with a singular hand, bringing his other to grab her jaw, forcing her face to the front where she'd have to look back up at him.

His eyes were demeaning, she hated the feeling of being this close with him. It only brought back old, unwanted, trashed memories that she wouldn't want to remember even on her death bed.

"I'm making it my business, sweet pea," he'd finally voiced, his eyes narrowed as she dared to look into them. The specs of brown mixed with gold in his irises seemed to intimidate her, much like his mint breathe that fanned her skin. She wanted nothing more than to knee him in the balls, but she couldn't.

He'd finally removed his hand from it's tight grasp on her jaw so she could speak clearly, "well, hate to break it to you, but it's not, and neither is anything else I partake in."

In that moment, her confident words could've been burnt to a crisp with the information Jisung bestowed. He actually had planned to tell her, which was the exact reason he cornered her in the hall in the first place. Although, as he stared down at her pissed expression, and remembered how his old buddy Na Jaemin was becoming rather well acquainted with her - something else came to mind.

He hid the devil-like grin that so badly wanted to show. Instead, he turned to the others, giving them a signal, before letting her go. Hyeyeon had immediately stepped many steps away from him and his friends after her hands had fell back to her side, her green eyes making sure to stay on him and his dogs. Weird, what the hell was the point of that?

"Fine," Jisung had casually hummed as he walked back up to where she was now standing in the school halls once again, towering over her with his height, "just don't drug him, now, you hear me?" he seemed to taunt her. He didn't wait nor allow her to even speak before he was walking away down the halls, right towards the exit to skip class, his members following right behind him.

The exasperated look that had spread over her face was enough for Jisung to know exactly what he wanted to do, and just how he was going to do it.

"You're a piece of fucking shit, Park Jisung!" the comment she yelled back at him as he was already at the exit doors only caused him to laugh. If only she knew how much she had in store for him, he thought humorously, holding up a middle finger but not even looking back as he pushed open the door. With that, Jisung was gone, probably going outside to smoke and do whatever else he did when he decided to become more of an imbecile - it disgusted her.

She could only stare at the door he and the others had just walked out of, trying to process if he really just did that. Right then, there was no doubt in her bones that she hated him, she fucking hated Park Jisung, and nothing could ever change that.

Chapter six; unexpected invites

Friday, she repeated the word in her head many times. Never did she think that a day of each week would mean so much to her, but no doubt Friday's were a blessing to the world. There was nothing she needed - and wanted - more than to go home before collapsing onto her bed, where she would proceed to sleep for the rest of the weekend.

It was the perfect plan, and she was damn determined to follow through with it.

Which was why she shot out of her seat the moment the bell rang, her feet like jet engines as she threw her bag over her shoulder. Hyeyeon was thinking aimlessly about sleeping so much, that she hadn't even bid Nana a goodbye. The boy had watched in confusion and defeat as she made a break for it out of the classroom, following all the other students eager to leave.

Jaemin blinked a few times, unsure of what to do then. There were many things he wanted to ask the girl he'd just met. Lots of things were spread around high schools, obviously, and it was pretty rare for them to ever be true. However, ever since he'd hung around with her, people had been telling him things - and they made no sense to him. Whenever he would ask, why do you think that? or why should I not be around her? they would refuse to answer. It was like the moment any question like that left his lips, their brains just turned off and they forgot the entire English language.

It all made zero sense to him. The more he hung out with Hyeyeon, the more he thought she was just a normal girl. So just what had she done to have the entire school against her?

To think, even Park Jisung warned him about her.

Determined to figure it out one way or another, he still felt an endless connection to the girl whom he'd only met yesterday. This is why his feet moved quicker than the thoughts going through his head as he threw his own bag over his shoulder, making his way out of the class and going after her.

Meanwhile, Hyeyeon took in the outside world's air as she stepped out of the school. Her green eyes looked upward towards the pretty sky, that was mainly crowded with many clouds, but it still managed to look gorgeous from down below. It seemed to brighten her mood even a little as she adjusted the bag on her shoulder, beginning to make her way towards the sidewalk, where she'd then begin her walk home.

Of course - she didn't do this until she pulled out her earbuds, plugging them into her phone. It was impossible for her to walk home without music blasting through her ears at full volume.

Shuffling her playlist, she immediately couldn't help but sing along to the words to the song Andromeda. Everything almost felt right as she disappeared into her own world, not even noticing the people that looked to her, before they'd turn away to whisper rumors and things to their friends. It was a common day for her, something she was far too used to after the events she'd never forget.

It was when she finally looked up, having just about to have stepped onto the sidewalk that led towards the street towards her house. Her glowing green eyes almost burst right out of their sockets at the sight of the vehicle that was parked at the curb in front of her at DMHS. It was quite the sight she hadn't expected to say the least - but what blew her mind even more - was who was leaning against the side of it.

Reaching up a hand, she ripped her earbuds out of her ears without even turning off the music. They fell limply at her sides and bounced against her as she broke into a run towards the person.
