pursing her lips as she thought about his words, and just what piece of shit he was talking about, Hye reached up to fix the Chanel sunglasses, making it where they weren't messing up her hair and sat perfectly atop her button nose. "Oh," she finally hummed, before turning around to look towards all the teenagers that stood in the front of the school. Out of the many, most of them had eyes on the two of them. Not caring much about that, however, she was only looking for one person in particular that happened to be her garbage ex boyfriend. After scanning the crowd, she turned back to him, "I don't think he's here."

He could only watch as she laughed with the mystery boy she was talking to, taking great note of his dark attire, tattoos, and bleached hair. It reminded him a lot of Jisung and his friends, surely she doesn't hang around with people like that.

"Alright, well, you and I are hanging out, and that's that," he concluded after a moment, already walking to the drivers side of the car, before he felt the need to add, "so get in, bitch."

From Jaemin's perspective, all his chocolate eyes witnessed was the girl he'd been planning to ask a particular question not even look his way, her eyes instead brightening as her lips parted and laughs escaped from her lips. He found himself sighing at the realization she seemed to be rather acquainted with whoever that was, and also at the fact he didn't get to ask her in the first place.

Shaking his head, he tried to cheer himself up. You barely know this girl, you can just ask on Monday, but still as he watched the bright red Toyota drive away from the high school, he heard her voice in his head, saying that certain nickname he hadn't heard anyone call him until he met her, Nana.

Jaemin had to walk home today, as he knew sure as hell he was not going to ask Jisung for another ride. As far as he was concerned, he didn't even want to be five centimeters with in him. The boy he knew as a kid had completely changed into someone he didn't want to be around. Being around Jisung and his friends for one car ride was enough for Jaemin to gather they were all involved in something bad. Bad as in illegal, and he couldn't be caught in things like that - not with his parents.

I really should get my license, he thought helplessly to himself as the red vehicle had eventually disappeared in the distance. The girl that had been in it left many questions floating in the air as she'd left, and he found himself contemplating almost all of them as he adjusted the strap of his backpack on his shoulder, beginning his way down the sidewalk.

Na Jaemin wasn't exactly a goody-two-shoes, but he was someone who tried his best not to get in trouble or do bad things. Although, sometimes when he was provoked - he couldn't help himself, as it was important to him to protect the one's he loved. The girl he'd met on his first day at such a place in Chicago took him by surprise. She'd been some sort of outcast, but there seemed to be nothing wrong with her in the first place. Jaemin didn't understand the jokes he heard people make to her, always being something about drugs. The looks she would get made no sense to him, and how people would cower when he'd ask them just exactly why they kept warning him about her.

He wasn't someone to be involved with bad things - at least, not purposely.

But this girl, this girl spiked his interest. Despite the fact that curiosity kills the cat, he wanted to figure out just what those jokes meant, and why the entire population of DMHS was against Kim Hyeyeon.

If that meant getting close to her first, so be it. A girl like that can't be involved in such things, right?

He sighed as he continued his way down the sidewalk. The sky seemed to be trying to tell him something as clouds seemed to gather in it, blocking the sun and making the entire world feel a bit darker from their actions. With fall being in session and winter coming upon them, he looked towards up above, wondering if it was going to rain once again. As if it'd almost match his mood.

Confusion spread over his expression as he pulled it out, merely from the fact he didn't keep in contact with many people. It wasn't like he didn't have friends, but ever since he'd moved from New York people seemed to forget about him. Although, on days like that day, he wished he still had all his old friends to rely on, and Jaemin couldn't help but think back to when Jisung was one of those old friends.

Jisung: jae, there's a party at my house tonight,
if ur not there i'm gonna beat tf out of u on monday
man. its @ 10 pm 😎

Every time Jisung texted he used emojis that made Jaemin want to slam his head into a brick wall. He walked into the yard of his home, still staring down at the bright screen before him and contemplating. A party? He realized then Jisung didn't know much about him anymore, since the last time they were friends was when they were kids, before he left. Long story short, he wasn't the biggest fan of parties. After all, he didn't like to get involved in bad things, and idiotic, teenage parties were exactly where said bad things happened.

Although, he went to a fair share of them in New York before he left. It wasn't on his own terms though, his friends had convinced him, as some sort of 'parting gift.'

Chapter seven; elders wise words

The sight of what felt like a thousand teenagers piling into his house was something Jisung was used to, and not to mention, adored. He'd thrown parties for a while now, as it felt like something he just had to do in the beginning, but now he enjoyed it more than anything. It made the entire school love him - and hate her more.

However, on a Friday night which he would usually be already taking pills and smoking, he found himself feeling rather anxious. Any feeling that wasn't stoned was something he hated, so the feeling of anxiety creeping up his spine was something he despised. This was why you'd find the boy not greeting the guests that were entering his house, but endlessly tapping on his phone, his thumbs angrily sliding across the screen as he composed many texts to Renjun.

What kind of fucking nerve does he have to not reply?! he thought in anger, one of his hands forming into a fist that wasn't holding his phone. Finally, with a deep breathe leaving his lips as if to calm himself, he decided to call the dark haired boy, holding his phone tightly to his ear so he could hear over the commotion that was already beginning.

Making his way to one of the back areas that was off limits so he could actually have some peace, Jisung fell back onto one of the sofas in the large dining room of his home. The ringing of the call seemed to be mocking him at that point as he let out a frustrated groan. If he doesn't answer this fucking call...

"hello?"

"Renjun, you fucking piece of shit."

The sound of him clearing his throat was heard through the line, along with background noise of what Jisung presumed was his shoes walking against gravel - most likely in an alley way, "huh, did I give you the wrong pick up? what's the problem?"

His tone was oddly joking, and the last thing he wanted to hear from his member right now. "Where the fuck are you?!"

Renjun seemed to internally sigh at the fact that once again, Jisung was mad about something. He had a pretty good feeling as to what that 'something' was, as well, all of the gang knew at this point. Any time Jisung was this stressed and anxious - or even sad - over something, it usually led back to her.

Knowing well enough not to mess with the leader when he was in this sort of state, he only hummed casually, "alright, calm down, I was doing business on the south side of town. Turns out there's a lot of customers here, I think I'll sell here a lot more often."

This would've been good news at literally any other time. But right then, Jisung could've cared less about anything other than his plan.

"Great - but I need you to get the fuck back here immediately, I need what you were going to fucking make me like right now."

There's a long pause on the other side of the line. Truthfully, the dark haired drug-dealer wasn't quite sure what to think about what he was hearing from the leader. Obviously, he remembered Jisung giving him orders about what he wanted made at tonight's party. It was the usual things he wanted at every single one, he'd figured. That was, until he'd been informed about a few that were a bit out of the ordinary.

By that, he meant highly addictive. They were the sort of drugs you'd take if you were desperate to just forget about all the problems in your life, looking for a way to escape. The same type that Jisung had taken all those years ago. Hell, sometimes taking them could even result in death, depending on the dose. Those years ago, Jisung had been happy the dose hadn't been heavy enough to damage him/

But the dose he was asking for in this batch - was enough to kill.

It wasn't that this worried Renjun, he could fucking care less about someone dying as long as it wasn't one of them. He was just confused. What was he trying to do? His curiosity was getting the best of him, and he couldn't help but endlessly wonder who such a dose would be for.

"Sorry, Jisung-ah," he'd hummed, pushing a strand of hair out of his face before hiking the duffle bag he had on his arm up to his shoulder. His sneakers clicked against the pavement of the concrete laid out in the alley way he was now making his way out of, "I didn't think it was that big of a deal."

There was a frustrated, heaving groan heard from Jisung. He definitely is serious about whatever this is, he couldn't help but think.

"No fucking shit it's a big deal, why would it not be since I asked you for such a large dose?!" for once, it was like Jisung was using his one brain cell to actually say something logical. That's how you knew whatever he was scheming was serious.

At the realization, Renjun had figured he better take the money and get the hell back. Although he wasn't sure if he even had the ingredients to make what his leader needed, he didn't feel like informing him of that. So he'd only let out a monotone hum, "alright, I'll be back shortly."

Jisung bit his lip as he heard the line go dead. I fucking swear, sometimes Renjun makes me want to point a gun at his head and blast out his brain, he thought angrily, spinning on his heel to make his way back where the entirety of the party was.

The flashing lights and sight of sweaty dancing was enough to make him feel better almost instantly. His brown eyes glanced every which way, sending that smile he was so well known for at everyone who greeted him as he passed. Girls swooned at the sight of him, and it was something that'd only made him feel more powerful than he already was.

"Hi, Jisung-ah!" they'd squeal as he passed, always stopping whatever they'd been doing whether it was making out with a stranger or gossiping to their friends.

He'd only nod in acknowledgement, continuing his way towards the door. Jisung had a set idea of what he was going to do in his mind, and he clearly had no clue if it was going to work - but that didn't mean he wasn't going to try. Like any other brainless teenager, he was especially known for not caring about anything and most of all, taking risks. It was like a hobby to him at that point, and right then, that's exactly what he was going to do.

It was when he had about to of headed straight outside to await his special guest. His large hand had hovered just above the golden door handle of the two story large confinement the gang lived in, when he felt someone lay a hand on his shoulder, preventing him from leaving.

His eyes narrowed immediately as he grew cautious. Jisung was no stranger when it came to reflexes and combat, and had whipped around at was basically mach speeds. He'd been prepared to beat the living shit out of whoever it had been, but that was before he actually saw who it was.

And when he did, it only caused him to grow annoyed much like he was with Renjun. The last thing he needed was for these idiotic baboons to continuously step in his way.

"What do you want?!" he'd screamed out of not only anger but also because of the loud music booming through out the stereo's that hung around the entire house.

His caramel locks flew gently down his forehead, and his daring brown eyes only quaintly glared into his. "Mark wants to talk to you," it was obvious he longed to throw some insult at him, but being of the power he held now - he knew he couldn't. So instead, he'd only kept that bored, disgusted expression on his face as he spoke.

Jisung sighed at the words that left his lips. "Seriously - for what?" he cursed out loud, and didn't speak another word to Donghyuck, instead pushing right past him, their shoulders clashing against each other as he immediately went for the stairs.

Meanwhile, the caramel boy only watched as he disappeared up them. Reaching up a hand, he brushed off the shoulder he'd dared to brush against, wincing as he did so. "Fuckwad," he mumbled in annoyance, shaking his head before tearing his eyes away from him. why did Mark have to give it to him out of all people?

As soon as he felt accomplished with his seemingly nice appearance, he'd turned on his heel, making his way out of the restroom after flicking off the light. So why was attending? He wasn't sure what the answer was. Na Jaemin had no idea what it was inside him that was telling him to go, stealing his mother's car keys, before slipping right out the front door.

"what's it for, Jisung?!" the once always calm hyung was far from such a thing now. His brown eyes dark and flaming, his fists were balled, slamming onto the desk he sat at repeatedly as he narrowed his orbs up at the boy who stood before him.

Any other person on the planet would be completely, utterly, horrified at the sight of someone like Mark yelling at them. However, the only person that wasn't phased would be well - no one other than Park Jisung. His arms were crossed over his chest, his chocolate eyes bored-ly staring up at the ceiling as he repeatedly brought his black lip ring in-between his teeth, playing with it as it was the only entertaining thing he had to do.

Jisung didn't care how many times this hyung yelled at him. Nothing he could say could stop him anymore, and it was the best feeling perhaps he'd ever imagined. He was the one who got to make the decisions, him.

at this point, he hadn't even been listening to whatever words were leaving Mark's lips. He was only thinking about more specific details of his plan, thinking of every possible thing that could happen - and how he could prevent it.

Through out this entire situation, he found himself wanting to laugh. This hyung was really shorter than him, he thought humorously, a small grin managing to find it's way onto his lips as he tried not to burst into hysterics. But the frustrated, flaming look the boy before him had on his face definitely wasn't helping his situation.

"Listen, I don't know what you're up to - and normally I wouldn't care - but right now is not the time to scheme, Jisung," his voice was dark as he narrowed his eyes at the younger before him, "I gave you my position as leader for a reason, because I know you're strong enough for it." Having had been pretty set on just going along with his plan, he was beginning to be curious about just what had him so out of line.

Before he could even finally give in and ask, Mark had spoken again. But his next words seemed to give him only a small puzzle piece of what he wanted.

"There's something dark coming, Jisung, and you have to be ready to face it."



Chapter eight; bad decisions

"This movie fucking blows," the brunette was complaining beside the tall, bleach haired teenage boy, her green eyes only half open at this point due to the exhaustion she was feeling from lack of sleep and the long week. She'd let out a long yawn, reaching out her small hand and breaking the perfect warmth the two of them felt under the blanket they shared to grab the bowel of popcorn from the coffee table.

Cheng had only watched her expression, one brow raised in not only confusion but question as she hadn't said another word after that statement. Instead, she'd only stuck her hand in the giant bowl of popcorn they'd made about an hour ago, before stuffing her face with it.

he found himself almost giggling at her, about to of gone back to watching Cars 3, when he heard a short sniffle come from his best friend that was cuddled up beside him.

Looking back to her, he couldn't help but pose the question, "if it blows, then why are you crying?" his tone dripped of confusion, and the girl had been stuffing her face with more popcorn, chewing it only about half before looking to him.

No doubt about it, there were clear tears in her eyes. He couldn't help but laugh then at the fact she was that soft.

"Because it's fucking emotional when Cruz wins the race, you emotionless fiend!" she shot at him, picking up a singular popcorn piece and chucking it at him. She'd intended to hit him and cause him to flinch, but Cheng had only tilted his head a bit, opening his mouth to catch the piece perfectly. He grinned after chewing it at how astonished she looked, as if she'd just seem something ground breaking, "fuck, didn't know you suddenly had such good reflexes."

"I told you I'm a genius now," he'd only said, but she'd just shook her head at him, turning back towards the TV to watch the movie.

It was peaceful - just the two of them sitting there on the sofa in the living room of the usually empty, dead feeling home she lived in. With her parents never being around, it almost got scary being stuck by yourself all the time. Especially with the fact she'd had no friends after everything happened, it was nice to finally have Cheng back by her side - for what she hoped was to stay.

She didn't care what it was the two of them did as long as they were together. Even if it was something as silly as just sitting around at 11 PM and watching children's movies, she didn't mind. For finally, she had someone to rely on, someone other than her own deafening thoughts.

It was the best feeling she'd felt in a long time.

The movie was nearing it's end only moments later when a long yawn had left the tiny girl's lips. With the lights being out and the only light illuminating them being from the television, it felt like the perfect atmosphere to pass out in. Not to mention how warm she felt with her best friend beside her, and covered in a heap of blankets.

Slowly but surely, her eyelids found their way over her eyes. It seemed like time for her to go into hibernation, although she hadn't planned to sleep just yet - after all, Cheng was still here and she wanted to spend more time with him. But her body, on the other hand, seemed to have different plans as if continued to bed and beg for her to fall into slumber.

It wasn't long until she did.

The long lived best friend found himself grinning as he looked down at her. It's nice to just be free for once, he found himself thinking as he'd looked away from her now peacefully sleeping body. For it was true he'd missed just getting to sit around and do nothing whenever he pleased with his best friend. Something that normal teenagers would do.

And despite the fact Cheng was about as far from a normal teenager as you could be, he welcomed the feeling of being one in that moment. No drugs, no guns, no blood.

Such a homey feeling made him feel tired, too. He'd felt pretty set on sleeping as well, remembering how he didn't have strict orders to be back until late morning. Relaxing further into the soft, plush sofa, his eyes felt content on closing at such a time. For the first time in so long, he could finally sleep calmly, as if the entire world was pausing just so he could have his placid time.

That was, until he felt the vigorous vibrating in his back jeans pocket. It'd woken him up like a flash at the realization he was suddenly getting a call, and no doubt, upset him more than anything. There was a very small amount of people who would be calling him, so he knew it couldn't be good - especially if he was receiving one when it was supposed to be his beloved free time.

Sneakily, Cheng managed to slip himself out from under the soft blanket his best friend was still passed out under. His feet tip toed across the room, and he made his way upstairs where him speaking to whoever the caller was wouldn't awaken the sleeping beauty below.

finally reaching a safe destination, he dared to hold the cell phone up in front of him. His brown eyes blinked a few times as he read the Caller ID, trying to make sure it was correct. Following a short sigh, he registered that it was no doubt, Doyoung. It was actually just a bit of a relief for it to be his good friend, and he'd only shrugged, figuring it must not be anything very serious as he slid his thumb across the screen to answer, before pressing the phone against his ear.

What he'd expected to hear was his friend laughing before he told him some stupid joke, or rambling about something stupid that Johnny did - again. However, what Cheng didn't expect nor want to hear was the sound of heavy, dis-taunt breaths, sounding as if he'd been either fighting off someone or running for his life.

Pressing the phone tighter against his ear as if trying to hear any sort of dialogue as to what was happening, he only heard indistinct yells. In blank confusion, he tried to piece together just what was going on. Did one of the jobs go wrong? That rarely ever happened - so what the hell is going on?

More yelling was heard on the other end of the line, and he was just about to call out Doyoung's name when a sharp bang was sent through instead. Even the piercing sound managed to hurt his ears through the phone, and he found himself wincing as he processed just what such a particular sound had been.

Almost feeling breathless himself, he finally called out to his friend, "Hello - Doyoung - are you okay?! What the hell is going on?!"

He wasn't greeted with an answer, but more of the sound of sneakers slapping against the pavement. You could tell there were multiple people running - but from what? Worriedly, he found himself shifting from one foot to the other as he repeatedly called out to his friend. To think I took one fucking day off.

Suddenly, it'd stopped, and his ears were greeted with more restless breathes. Finally, a few coughs were heard, and the sound of his hyung's voice finally broke through, "Win, y-you need to get here now."

"What's happening, Doyoung?!" he demanded for what felt like the thousandth time, desperately trying to piece anything together. There were no other dangerous gangs in the area, and they never had any trouble with their assassinations. Why was this happening?

The thought of Hyeyeon's ex-boyfriend and his imbecile friends made a brief appearance in his thoughts. No, Cheng immediately dismissed such a thing being possible, there's no fucking way those idiots even know how to hold a weapon.

Although he told himself this, he couldn't be too sure. After all, there weren't any other people that would cause trouble with them - or even knew of them in the first place - not in this area. They made sure to keep their traces hidden with every step they took, never leaving a footprint uncovered. The thought that someone had actually found them was absurd.

However, that absurd thought had become his reality in less than a millisecond as he heard Doyoung cough out tiredly on the other line, "it's Kun - he's been shot."

"I really shouldn't be drinking tonight," he finally cleared his throat, informing Jisung, who wasn't standing close by him anymore due to the fact he'd walked to speak to someone across the room to grab a cigarette. He returned moments later with it dangling from his lips, having hadn't heard what he even said in the first place.

The tattooed boy inhaled the smoke, closing his eyes for a split second as if to cherish it like some sort of blessing. He'd exhale it, creating a cloud of white in the air right in Jaemin's face, before raising a brow, "sorry, what'd ya say?"

Trying not to show how annoyed he already was with him in such a short amount of time, he repeated once again, "I said, I really shouldn't be drinking tonight, I'm driving," he had to raise his voice over the booming bass of the music that played. By the time he finished his sentence, Jisung was staring at him like he was some sort of mental patient.

That was, before he burst out laughing. It was probably the most disturbing, fake laugh Jaemin had ever seen in his life, as the boy before him had been 'laughing' so hard he was bent over on his knees, slapping them repeatedly like he just couldn't believe it.

Such a sight was short lived as he'd stood up again, "you're funny, Jae."

But when his expression didn't change, Jisung realized just how serious he was. Snorting, he scoffed in disbelief, "what the fuck kind of guy turns down a drink?"

One who actually has a brain cell.

"Don't be a pussy, you got this far."

Heaving out a sigh, his words somehow managed to anger him more than he planned for them to. "Fine, but I'm not having more than one."

Chapter nine; hired help

His breathe ragged as his foot slammed against the break of his toyota, the car screeching as it abrubtly came to a halt against the curb. With the breathe's growing heavier upon each movement he made, this wasn't because he was crying. Sicheng didn't cry, but the breathes leaving his lips were that of extreme anger.

You couldn't just shoot one of them and get away with it. It was rare for anyone in the entire city of Chicago to even know of them in the first place, and the one's who did knew not to cross their path. They were feared - and for good reason. If you even so attempted to mess with one of them, your death would be imminent.

Which was why Sicheng was prepared to kill anyone who got in his way of getting to his friends - scratch that - his family. His hands were quick as he reached into the middle compartment of the vehicle, pulling out the weapon he always kept there. The silver of the pistol he had as a safety precaution glowed under the light coming from the ceiling of his car, and he'd heaved out a heavy breathe as he tucked it into the pocket of his leather jacket.

The details he'd received from Doyoung hadn't been that specific, but hopefully he thought they were enough to get him to the right place. It was on the south side of Chicago, which was specifically their turf. The drug business always thrived here, and it a good source of the money they received monthly - after the assassinations - if there were any other gangs in the area, they made a horrible decision to cross into such territory. Especially now if one of them had the guts to shoot one of them. Sicheng, and no doubt the others, would chase whoever's gang it was to the other side of the world until they had the satisfaction of slowly running a knife across their throat or perfectly skimming a bullet right into his skull. One or the other would do, and he would make sure of it.

When Sicheng had left the house of his best friend, he hadn't thought much of her being confused when she awoke. This is firstly due to the fact it'd probably most likely be awhile, since when she naps, it's for about an entire century. It wasn't like anything bad would happen to her in that amount of time. No one knew about him and her in this area that would do anything dangerous to her, and Jisung was probably too busy on a Friday night to think about messing with her. She was fine.

He'd just tell her something with his family that was an emergency came up - which wouldn't be a lie.

Only moments later he'd broke into a run, making his way through the alleyway of the downtown south of Chicago. It was past midnight then, meaning the only source of light he had was from the street lights that lined the road, which was far behind him now as he proceeded deeper into the narrow alley.

He'd been here plenty of times, though, so it was no issue finding his way even in the dim lights. This is why Sicheng continued to run, peeking every corner he passed for any sign of someone he didn't know - which would be shot on sight.

His hand hovered over his jacket pocket where the gun was safely tucked, and he went and went. Although it was difficult, he refused to worry of what might have happened to his friends. There was no way anyone else got hurt, they're too good at what they do to.

But what if the enemy was better?

"fuck," he mumbled in a whisper aloud to himself, scolding himself mentally for thinking like that. That's impossible for anyone to be better than us.

His sneakers scraped against the wet pavement that still wasn't dry from the previous rain storms happening recently. Brown eyes filled with curiosity, he finally reached the end of the alley way that led into another that was a long, gravel road that went through the middle of the town. This was where most of the business was done.

Due to the dark, as he peered into it it'd taken him a minute to register that there were people taking cover behind something. His eyes blinked as they tried to adjust to the light, and it was then that he recognized them.

"Doyoung, Johnny!" he whisper-yelled to them, causing the two that had been ducking behind a dumpster's heads to whip to them. They both had their own weapons held tightly in their grasps - and he didn't see anyone else in sight - so why were they hiding?

They also looked to be the only ones there. No sight of Kun - who'd apparently gotten shot - was seen, and he hoped that the others had gotten him out safely. Although it was weird that Taeyong wasn't around. The leader never left a fight.

At the sight that whoever the enemy was was gone, Sicheng had only stepped out one foot when the two had called to him, "get back - there's a sniper!"

Thanks to his fast reflexes, he'd brought his foot back into safety behind the wall of the alleyway he'd came from. As if on queue, the sound of a shot rung through the air, hitting the ground where his foot had been only a millisecond ago. His eyes widened a bit as he stared at the hole the tiny sniper bullet had made in the gravel, his eyes looking back up to his friends.

This was a sticky situation indeed. "who the hell is it?" he whisper yelled the question to the boys.

"we don't know, we weren't able to catch any names," Doyoung had replied in the same low tone back so only he could hear, "apparently someone else has been selling on our turf, Kun's the only one who saw him."

A deep breathe left Sicheng's lips as Doyoung had then informed him that Yuri and Jaehyun had taken him to the hospital. But they still hadn't explained where Taeyong was.

When he'd asked, they said they didn't know. Weird.

"what's the plan?" he'd mouthed only moments later.

Doyoung only shrugged, and it was then Johnny had yelled as loud as he could seem to muster, keeping his gun gripped tightly in his hand, "hey, come out you fucking pussy and fight us face to face!" he'd screamed to whoever dared to begin such a thing in the first place. The three of them then waited for any response.

Nothing, they waited a bit longer - but whoever had the audacity to start this seemed to afraid. They should be.

Feeling anger rise up his entire body, spiraling through his veins like venom, Sicheng couldn't take it anymore. His other two friends still hiding behind the dumpster's eyes bulged as he stepped out into the open of the long, wide alleyway. His sneakers crinkling against the gravel as he loudly stepped out, right in the middle, raising his hands in the air as if he was surrendering.

"what the fuck are you doing, Win?!"

He ignored the calls from his friends, instead raising his arms up higher and waving them around. A smirk spread over his lips as he awaited any sign of a bullet, "come on, shoot me, I dare you!"

The dark of the night seemed to be the only thing that was responding to him though. There was a long silence, when the sound of something opening. His eyes narrowed at the sight of a person walking out of the building he then assumed the shot had come from. However, they hadn't sported a sniper - but instead an AK - as they held it in front of them cautiously. He realized then, he didn't recognize whoever this person was - and the way they were dressed made no fucking sense.

He felt himself growing rather suspicious as his hands gently fell to his sides. The person still didn't speak, and they stopped about fifteen feet away from him.

"who the fuck are you?!" Sicheng hadn't waited to demand them.

"that's not your business, but I'd hate to tell you this turf isn't yours anymore," the mysterious, casually dressed boy had said. Although when the words fell from his lips they sounded highly forced, as if he was some sort of broken record or a failing actor.

Sicheng watched as he dared to raise the gun once again, pointing straight at him. In that moment, he'd been about to pull out his own weapon - as it was obvious this kid was some sort of fake, or just really bad at whatever he was doing. He most likely would've gotten the shot off first thanks to his quick reflexes, but before he could even merely think of doing such - the sight of someone running up behind him, a knife in hand as they went. It was a sight he'd seen many times, and probably should've expected - as the platinum haired boy had wrapped his arm around the boys neck, whispering something that was inaudible to everyone else in his ear before he casually ran the sharpened metal of the knife across his throat. The way he performed this was like he'd done it everyday, as his movements seemed like that of some sort of ninja out of one of those anime's. It made Sicheng almost laugh as the boy had coughed, struggling for a second before he fell limp to the ground.

The red substance known as blood poured from the deep wound across his throat, creating a puddle that Taeyong had mindlessly stepped right over. Dressed in all black, he took off the mask that was covering his face as he walked up to the three that were now all standing in the middle of the alleyway.

"how long were you hiding back there?" Johnny had asked in confusion as soon as their leader was standing right before them.

Taeyong only shrugged, "Ever since a bit after I got the call." He'd sighed helplessly then, before chucking what looked like some sort of card at them. Doyoung had been the one to pick it up first before it'd dangled through the air onto the ground, and he held it in the air for the three of them to see what it was.

The only thing that was written on it had been two letters.

JN

"It was a cover up, that's not the guy with the sniper," Taeyong had noticed Johnny's blank expression, as he had been the only one who hadn't put the obvious puzzle pieces together, "he was hired to cover when the sniper dipped."

"Ohhh," the idiotic boy had hummed in final understanding.

"JN?" Doyoung repeated the two letters that were written, his brain working quickly, "initials, I'm assuming."

Taeyong had only nodded, having already gathered this information. His hand reached up to run through his white colored hair, his teeth pulling at one of his snake bites as he then commanded, "Johnny, go to the hospital to check up on the others," the boy had only nodded, already leaving on the way to do as he was told. He'd then looked to the other two that stood there, "You two, head back home. Research everything possible," he'd already begun walking away from the way he'd came, probably going to hide the body and cover every single trace possible that could've been left, "figure out who the fuck did this."

As you could imagine, it was like lifting the entire earth before she managed to get him inside the house. All the while, Jaemin kept mumbling dumb shit she couldn't seem to comprehend as she carried him to the sofa she had been peacefully napping on only hours ago.

Dropping him on top of the blanket, he coughed a bit as his back hit the soft fabric. A sigh left her lips as she watched him stare blankly at the ceiling, shaking her head before rushing to the kitchen to grab him a glass of water.

Jesus fuck, she couldn't help but think as she was returning with it moments later, why did Jisung do this to him? she thought with a frown, and it was something she found herself debating on for a while. It sure didn't seem like the two of them were friends, and being that he just moved, they couldn't have really had any beef yet.

Was it because of me? the thought was horrifying to her. Although she was unaware of just what they did to him, she had a good feeling it had a bit to do with drugs in his drink. From the way it seemed, Jisung had been trying to do something not pleasant to the poor boy.

She only realized that her accusation was even more accurate when she remembered what he'd said to her in the hallway - speaking specifically of Jaemin.

Oh my god, she could almost feel tears rising to her eyes from how bad she felt, it really is my fault. It was completely like Jisung to do something like this - his hobby was practically ruining her life. Of course he would start messing with someone he knew she was becoming acquainted with.

Dully exhaling, she tapped Jaemin's shoulder, causing him to glance over to her. Holding out the glass, she hummed, "here, drink this."

He'd sat up slowly but surely to grab the glass of water. His hand had been a bit shaky as he drank it, and as he did so, she'd fell to sit on the couch beside him.

There was a long silence, but by his movements and breathing pattern she could tell he was already getting better - from the alcohol at least. She didn't know much about him, but she had gathered the fact he seemed to have a high alcohol tolerance.

"you weren't there," his voice finally cut through the quiet.

His words caused her gaze to snap to him almost instantly, her brows furrowing in confusion, "what? what do you mean?"

Finishing the glass of water, Jaemin had set it down on the coffee table before them before sitting back again. "Jisung s-said you'd be there - that's why I went, I went for you," the drugs were obviously still fucking with him. So it did have to do with her.

Although, something about what he'd said still confused her, "why would you go because of me?" she couldn't help but ask instead of telling him that had been a lie. Of course, you obviously couldn't listen and believe what he was saying since he was obviously not in the right state of mind, but she still wanted to try asking.

Jaemin had looked over to her, his bloodshot eyes blinking a few times as he stared into hers. Under his gaze, she couldn't help but feel a bit intimidated - and even nervous - as she awkwardly cleared her throat, refusing to make eye contact.

"I wanted to ask if you wanted to hang out this weekend."

She had to think for a moment in order to process his words. "That's - why did you just ask me at school?" she frowned harder realizing the entire story, "Nana, I wasn't even going to go to the party, Jisung lied."

Due to how his mind must be messing with him and his thoughts being off, he couldn't seem to understand. "T-Then how were you there?"

She chuckled at how he was acting, only because his tone of voice was that of a kid. Finally, she sighed, "I went for you."

Not even a second after the words left her lips, he was staring at her again. His eyes bored into hers like the sunset against the ground on a Summer day, and she found herself gazing right back at him. It was when Nana grew closer to her that she quickly leaned back, unsure of what he was trying to do. But his face kept coming and coming, until their noses were almost touching and she could feel his breathe fanning her skin.

The scent of his cologne was burned into her nostrils as she saw the sight of his pretty brown orbs up close. "Whoa there, Nana," she coughed a bit in worry, a hand going to his chest where she gently pushed him back, "you're high, and you need sleep."

She was unaware of the sad look that was on his face as she rose to her feet, turning back to him, "I'll be here when you wake up, okay? You'll probably have an awful headache, but at least you'll be back to normal."

He'd only stared up at her for a moment, before nodding in agreement, "if you say so, noona."

Laughing a bit at the name, she realized how messed up he really was. "Jaemin, I'm younger than you," but he was already passed the fuck out. The sight of him so abruptly sleeping was surprising to her, as she blinked down at him a few times, trying to process how that was even possible. Whatever drug they put in his drink must have really high effects of exhaustion.

Yet another sigh left her lips as she made her way upstairs to shower and do other things. There was no telling how long it would be until he woke up, but it would probably be a long while until late morning, even. this meant she could probably get some well deserved sleep, too. It wasn't like that short ass nap earlier had been enough.

She found herself going on her phone as she awaited for the water to warm up, leaning against her bathroom counter. This was after she had played music, of course, and the sound of Bang Bang Bang echoed through the almost empty feeling home as she noticed a new notification on Instagram.

Due to the fact everyone at school hated her and she was really inactive, she didn't usually receive those.

leehyuck has followed you

She was lost, to say the least. This was because she had no fucking clue who that was. The name didn't sound familiar to her, and she'd tapped on the person's profile in confusion.

Their profile picture wasn't their face - unfortunately. It was just some blurry photo of what looked like - Michael Jackson? Her brows furrowed as she only grew more confused, seeing their profile was private so she couldn't stalk their posts.

Unfortunately, the only thing she had of this random person was the name that displayed beside their picture. Lee Donghyuck.

Huh, never heard that name before, she thought blankly. Figuring it was some random person that didn't even live in the area, she mindlessly requested to follow them back like a kind person, before closing out of the app. Turning off her phone, the next song on her playlist had already begun, and she found herself dramatically acting as if she was singing Supremacy whilst digging through her closet for clothes to wear after she got out of the shower.

Her shower was spent with her screaming the lyrics to Muse songs at the top of her lungs. Running her hands through her hair as she made sure to get all the conditioner out, she only continued to boast the lyrics from her mouth. No doubt Nana would be passed out for a while so hard that not even her loud, passionate excuse of singing could wake him up.

Knowing this well enough, she felt as if each droplet of water washed away one of her many worries in life. All the things that had been bothering her - even Jisung - seemed to disappear with in those short moments.

However, she should've known how short lived her joyous moments would be at the sound of her phone letting out a high-pitched ding.

There was of course, the hope that it was just Sicheng. But something inside of her had a feeling like after the previous events, there would definitely be a certain someone texting her.

This was only proved to be further correct once she unlocked it, leaning a bit out of the shower to peer down at the screen.

Why did Jisung do these things? It was such a question she'd been asking for years ever since it all happened. Why did he turn on her like that when all she had ever wanted was to help him? Never would his mind set make sense to her, and it only hurt her to think of all the moments with him she had previously cherished.

The old Park Jisung was long gone, she had to remind herself, and he was never coming back. It was almost insane to witness someone you were once so in love with change into a completely new, unrecognizable person - not only by appearance, but by personality as well.

Although it'd been years now, and she swore she was more than used to what her life had come to be now. As she thought and thought about how easy it all used to be, when she always felt safe everywhere she went because she had him and Chengie always by her side. Back when the entire school didn't look down on her life she was some sort of mental patient, but cheered her on and squealed about how 'perfect' the two of them were together.

These thoughts, for some reason, found themselves cycling around her mind. And as she managed to finally fall asleep that night, a tear somehow managed to slip out of the corner of her right eye. Wiping it away furiously, she angrily slapped herself mentally. Stop thinking about it, and found herself praying that through out all the hardships in her life, Jaemin would be okay.

Sicheng was frustrated. There were too many things on his mind on such a night, too many questions he was unable to answer were floundering his brain, making his head ache. He'd given up on the search finally at 3 AM, sitting in the comfort of his bed and leaning his back against the headboard.

Kun and the others had gotten back about an hour after him and Doyoung had given up for tonight on the research. They'd desperately wanted to ask him questions even though from the shape he seemed to be in, they knew it wouldn't be a good idea from how weak he was feeling. At the sight of him walking limply into the room, his shoulder (where he was shot) all wrapped up in a cast, before they had even been able to say hello, Yuri had already snapped at them, "don't you fucking dare start parading him." They knew well enough to listen, and had let it go for then.

At this time, everyone in the house was well past passed out. He knew he should be, too. But there were too many thoughts crowding his usually sunny mind, and it was causing him to be rather stressed as he could only sit there, staring into the darkness.

The sound of the same whooing owls in a tree somewhere outside his window felt as if they were mocking him with each whoo. Something so small managed to bother him then as he stared out the window across the room, the stars twinkling from the high, night sky above.

Na Jaemin, he didn't know anything about the boy his best friend had met so suddenly that day. Although, he remembered clearly how rare it was for anyone to be how she had explained Jaemin to be and not be involved in the dark side of Chicago. After all, even she didn't know where he came from or why he moved at the end of October. And frankly, he found even that rather suspicious.

That, and it was also the fact that his name perfectly fit. Whether it was just his first name using the first and last letter, or the first initial of his first name and the first initial of his last name. He remembered clearly how Doyoung couldn't find a lead on him when he had asked the first day Hyeyeon told him about Jaemin, but was it possible that like 127, he too was a professional at covering his tracks?

These are the many things that fought their way into his skull as he fell asleep on such an eery Friday night. Sicheng figured he should get a good night's sleep, because he knew exactly where he was heading first thing in the morning.


Chapter twelve; sensitive subject

It was around half past 2 in the afternoon when the green eyes of the dark haired girl finally fluttered open. A long yawn left her lips as she slowly sat her body up in the comfort of her duvet, her eyes blinking a few times before grazing across her room. It was then, on a seemingly nice Saturday afternoon, she felt actually well rested for once.

Although, she'd had no idea what time it even was and how long she'd genuinely slept until she had turned on the phone that had sat on her nightstand. The memories of last night slowly flooded through her brain as she saw the numbers at the top of the screen.

Oh fuck, she hadn't planned to wake up this late, not with the boy that was sleeping downstairs. The once calm feeling she had felt while sitting up and stretching was long gone as she hurriedly threw the duvet off her body, throwing her legs over the side of her bed. Next thing you'd know, she was running full speed for the steps, trying to make sure her hair didn't look like a complete rat's nest on the way.

Maybe he left already, she was thinking as she was padding like a mad man down the stairs. It wasn't like she knew what kind of drugs they'd put in his drink to know what the side effects were, or if they'd have him either woke as hell or passed out for like - an entire day. Honestly, now that she thought about it, she didn't know anything about that stuff in general. Despite living in Chicago, her parents had never allowed her near things like that for her to ever learn about it from a young age.

Her thoughts were cut off by the scent of - pancakes? Slowly padding across the carpet of the living room once she reached the bottom of the stairs, she looked to the couch where the boy had been passed out only to see he wasn't there anymore.

A strange feeling egged it's way up her spine as her feet were right by the doorway that led into the giant kitchen in her home. Peeking her head through it, she held onto the doorway with her hands to fully peer into the kitchen.

It was when her green eyes were met with the sight of Na Jaemin, bent over the stove, and casually flipping fucking pancakes, like what happened last night just hadn't. Such a thing she was witnessing caused her to blink a few times in confusion, trying to understand if it was really real. He was still dressed in the apparel from last night, except he'd taken his bomber jacket off and thrown it over the back of the couch in the living room, leaving him standing there in a black Nirvana tee and ripped skinny jeans. With those same dangling earrings he always wore, his hair was a mess atop his head as he'd only continued, humming a song she didn't recognize to himself, having no fucking cares in the world.

"Uh," she almost felt awkward speaking up, catching his attention as his head glanced up to her, and that bright grin spread over his lips. It was then she didn't actually know what question out of the many she should even start with. "How are you feeling?"

He'd cleared his throat, flipping the last finished pancake onto the plate he had set out beside the stove. Jaemin flicked off the switch to turn it off, before leaning against the counter and crossing his arms over his chest, shrugging as he hummed, "I'm okay, I had a mad headache when I woke up though, but luckily," he paused to walk over, opening a cabinet and motioning to the many assortments of medicines that laid inside, "I found your medicine cabinet."

No doubt, she still felt rather confused, "um, do you remember anything?"

Perhaps this had been a bad question to ask from the look that spread over his expression. It was a look of uncertainty, that had only seemed to last for a short bit as he diverted his eyes from her to the ceiling in thought. "A bit, I just remember Jisung convinced me to go to some stupid party, and I got messed up out of my own idiocy, I guess," he explained everything he knew slowly, "and then, apparently you saved me, Yeonnie, my white knight," he added as a joke, snickering at himself while she only cringed.

"Please never say that again." She couldn't believe how he was so laid back in times like this. He really has no idea what Jisung did, she tried not to show how upset that made her. In a way, it could be seen as good thing - as it was all her fault that now Jisung was trying to mess with Jaemin, just like her. But at the same time, it was his right to know.

"Sorry," he'd said playfully, before turning towards the pancakes he'd made, "I'm assuming you like pancakes since you had a whole five boxes of mix in your pantry, so as a thank you for saving my dumb ass I made you some." He'd picked up the plate of pancakes, that were nicely set atop each other, butter on top, and held it out to her.

Staring at the plate in his hand, she raised a brow, "I love pancakes, and you're welcome - but, don't you want to eat, too?" it was crazy to her how he was acting after having been so fucked up off of the alcohol and whatever drug he'd been given. How could just some medicine suddenly make him perfectly fine? What kind of tolerance does this guy have?!

However, Jaemin only shook his head vigorously, walking forward to set the plate in her hands. As he did this, he'd been so close the tips of her feet were touching his sneakers, and the close proximity reminded her of yet another thing that had almost happened last night.

He'd tried to kiss her.

A suddenly nervous feeling shot throughout her veins, and it was one she wasn't used to. Without another thought, she took the plate, practically shooting towards the table to sit down. Jaemin had noticed how quickly she had scurried away from him, looking at her a little confused.

She was staring at the plate before her, grabbing the syrup that was set in the middle of the table. Pouring some over her pancakes, she'd begun eating when she felt his eyes on her again. Growing uncomfortable, she looked up to meet his soft gaze, "are you sure you don't want any?"

His eyes went from her, to the plate that was in front of her. In reality, Jaemin wouldn't tell her - but his head did still hurt quite a lot. He'd had a fair amount of hangovers, so his alcohol tolerance was irregularly high. So for him to actually feel this way meant whatever he drank last night must've been strong.

Although, he'd never felt a hangover quite like this, there was something different.

Shrugging, he'd made his way across the room to slide in the booth that was for the table. He was rather close to her, and she tried to act like this was no big deal. That was, until swiftly, he'd reached out to take the fork she'd been using right out of her hand, before cutting off a piece of the pancake and slipping it in his mouth.

Eyes wide, she'd only washed in surprise. When she asked if he wanted any, she didn't mean for him to do that. Finding herself coughing a bit, she tried to regain her normal composure, "hey, you fucker, I never said you could use my fork."

He took another bite of the pancake, chewing and swallowing the delicious breakfast food before smiling down at her from his outstanding height, "whoops, my bad."

Shaking her head, she found herself smiling as she took the fork back from him. For some reason, she'd be bothered a lot by anyone else doing this.

Somehow, though, with Jaemin it almost felt - normal?

"So, do you usually attend Jisung's parties? I thought you hated him," only moments later, the caramel haired boy was making talk with her as she continued to eat - well, with him stealing her fork and grabbing a bite himself every so often.

The question caused her body to grow tense again, and from how close he was sitting to her she hoped he didn't notice. I should probably tell him, she realized, clearing her throat and setting the fork down so she could look to him.

Jaemin grew confused by her suddenly serious expression as she'd turned to face him. He only stared into her deep eyes that much reminded him of his favorite season - spring. Such a warm, green color that brought back memories of the blooming trees back in New York, and it was something he'd get lost in every once in a while.

"Nana, there's something I have to tell you."

His ears perked up at such words leaving her lips, and it was almost as if he was hoping to hear something.

"Uh," she awkwardly stumbled over her words, as if it was hard for her to say. This only caused his hopes and curiosity to rise as he stared down at her with those warm, chocolate orbs of his.

"Listen, I only went to the party because Jisung told me you were there and that something happened," she began, her voice a bit shaky as each word left her lips surely, "long story short, you didn't get drunk or anything out of 'your own idiocy,' Jisung had been trying to do something to you - I-I don't know what but - he drugged your drink, Jaemin."

Her words were almost foreign to him as he could only stare in astonishment. His eyes widened a bit as he put the pieces together in his brain, and it was then that he almost felt angry, and no doubt betrayed, by someone who was something to be his friend.

Although she could of been lying, something inside him made him trust the small girl he'd only met days ago, and he found himself making sense as to just why the hangover had felt so weird this morning.

"why would he do that?" his voice had been a mumble as he looked away in thought.

"because of me," is all she replied, nothing more being said from her lips. He'd looked back to her to see if she had really been serious, only to see she'd risen from her feet, walking out of the room and back into the living room.

He couldn't help but remember all those things people told him about her, all the warnings he would get since everyone seemed to know the two of them were becoming friends. Something inside of him forced him to get up, following her into the living area of her home.

All those things that people said, always had something to do with Jisung. He knew it then, and the dying confusion and curiosity is what caused him to speak up as he was standing behind her, her back to him as she stared towards the blank television screen, "Hyeyeon, just what happened between you and Park Jisung?"

It was a deafening question, one that caused her to wince at the sound. She didn't know what all of the horrid emotions she was feeling then was about, but she did know she didn't want to feel them anymore.

She'd turned back to him, with his jacket in hand. Stepping forward towards him, she held it out to him to take, but he wasn't paying any attention to the belonging of his that lay in her hands. He was focused on the tears that were welled in her eyes, and something inside him seemed to understand that there was no way any of those things the people told him were true. For then, it was clear that the only emotion she was feeling thanks to such a thing he had asked caused nothing more than remorse and hurt, and it was the last thing he knew she deserved to feel.

Park Jisung had did something to this girl, and from what he now knew he tried to do to him, he believed it.

"I think you should go," her voice was a mere whisper as she held the jacket out to him, stretching her arms further. More tears were welling up in her eyes, tears of guilt for what she felt she was causing to this innocent boy, and she couldn't manage to even look at him then, instead diverting her green irises to the floor.

She waited, she waited for him to take the jacket and for the weight to be lifted from her hands which it laid in. But it never happened, and she began to feel pressured under that gaze of his that held so much in-explainable power. She knew he would ask such a question sooner or later, and now that he had, she couldn't answer it.

The longer she stood there, the more she felt like crying. And it was a feeling she fucking despised. She hadn't cried in years, it was something she never did even after everything that had happened to her. So why was she crying now? Why had her seemingly in-breakable shell suddenly shattered?

"Yeonnie," his voice had trailed off as it left his lips, but she'd only stepped forward again to harshly push the jacket into his arms. The action caused Jaemin to frown, as she'd only swiftly turned on her heel, walking away from him into another room.

He only watched her leave, the feeling of hurt now rising up his veins, as well. Perhaps it would've been better for him to stay confused, and he realized that as he took the keys to his mother's mustang out of his jacket pocket, before dully making his way towards the front door of the home.

Opening the door to her house, he had only been staring back at where she'd left to. A part of him kept hoping she would run out of wherever she went, calling to him. Why? he wasn't sure, he wasn't really sure what he hoped for her to say to him. Or maybe he was just refusing to admit it.

Either way, he couldn't deny the unpleasant feeling that had taken place in his brain as he stepped outside, closing the door behind him. Even when he had climbed in his car he still found himself staring at the front door, just hoping.

But it never happened.

As he finally started the vehicle, placing his foot against the petal and driving off down the street, he then decided to try and focus on whatever story he would make up to his mother. But even then, she still found a way on his mind again.


Chapter thirteen; debt

"oh my - can someone get him to shut the fuck up? His retardation is giving me a headache," Yuri was complaining as she motioned to no one other than Johnny, who was standing on the kitchen table. Some random song from one of his playlist's was blasting from the stereo that hung on the wall, and Johnny was doing a really poor impersonation of the singer, belching out the lyrics like a crazy person while he spun in circles, waving his arms like what she herself would recognize as a fucking monkey.

Sicheng was sat on the opposite side of where Yuri was, and he only watched his stoned friend dance around and sing, a sigh leaving his lips. "I don't think anyone can stop him, unless you take away his weed."

Her eyes had widened suddenly at his words, and she pointed one of her long, black fingernails at him, "you're a genius, Winnie."

But the blonde-haired boy had only stared back at her in confusion, "what - I didn't even-," he had begun to say, but was cut off when she rose to her feet, walking to stand in front of the boy on the table.

Johnny hadn't even merely looked her way, until she had cleared her throat to scream at the top of her lungs, "JOHNNY, I'M GOING TO FUCKING BURN YOUR WEED!"

As the sound of these words, he'd tried to jump off the table as she had moved away. All the while, he was sputtering something around "oh my god no, please don't do it. is this a nightmare? someone pinch me," as he had jumped. His seemingly attempt at landing, however, went incredibly wrong when he ended up on his ass against the cold tile.

Sicheng winced at the sight, that must of fucking bruised. But Johnny hadn't even seemed to care about that as he shot to his feet, chasing after the girl who was already walked into the living room, "PLEASE DON'T DO IT, I NEED MY - I MEAN, IT HAS SO MUCH TO LIVE FOR!"

Cringing at the events that were happening, he distracted himself by the yelling that had only continued by staring out the window. Things had been rather hectic around the 127 house after the shooting had went down. Taeyong was more angrier than anyone - even Yuri - about someone else selling on what everyone knew as their territory. The fact that someone had the audacity to shoot one of them, had the leader flaming. Every time you would see him he either had his head in something on his computer or a book, trying to gather someone about those two letters that had been on that note. If not doing that, he would be going out for a job, seeming to kill out of complete cold blood. He had done this many times before, going to do assassinations just out of anger. And everyone knew you did not mess with him when he was going through one of these times unless you wanted to be hung on a platter, as well.

Much like his leader, Cheng was angry as well. He just couldn't get the thought out of his mind. The only lead he - or anyone had - right now was that boy. Although, there might of been other reasons he was targeting him, he didn't know. Either way, something about it just made sense.

He hadn't told the others about this yet, though. As he had planned to go to Hye's once he woke up, but he found himself getting distracted. Now, here he was, sitting in the kitchen and getting lost once again.

A sigh left his lips as he finally rose to his feet, deciding he was going to her house once and for all. If he was going to tell her, probably not. But he felt like some time with his best friend was a bit overdue.
