Her eyes were glued to the screen, but after hearing what he'd said, she'd looked to him with tears already flowing down her cheeks due to the scene that was playing. Holding out a hand, she motions towards the screen, "I'm sorry - do you not find this fucking emotional? The dog died!"

He had only glanced from her and her puffy, red cheeks, to the screen where the film Dog Days was playing. "I mean, yeah, it's super sad, but I've never seen even you cry this much over a movie," was all he'd said as she'd broke into even more tears at the sound of the nurse singing Amazing Grace to the guy who had just lost his dog.

"Fuck, I hate this!" she complained, sniffling angrily and turning away from the movie. Sicheng was almost astonished at how much she was crying as he held out the bag of Takis for her as if to make her feel better.

One thing about his best friend was that she definitely had a soft spot in her heart for animals. Which wouldn't be a bad gift idea for her, with her being a lonely bitch and all.

Through out the entire movie, she'd ended up crying over the smallest things. It was like everything was either a mindblowing miracle or a sob story to her, and it was almost infatuating to watch as he kept glancing over to watch her expressions.

Suddenly, her phone had vibrated beside her, causing her head to abruptly whip to look at it.

leehyuck:
you're so pretty. I think I'm lost in your eyes.

Blinking a few times, she had to pick up the phone and hold it in front of her face so that she could make sure she was reading such a DM correctly. Sure enough, it was from that person - well, guy - who she had no clue as to who he was.

Unsure as he could be some sort of pedophile or stalker, she pursed her lips, trying to decide if she even wanted to respond. Clicking on his profile, he hadn't even accepted her follow request yet, weird as fuck.

A small part of her thought hey, maybe it's the cute guy from the cafe. But that wouldn't make any fucking sense.

kimhyeyeon:
uh, thank you, stranger!! :)

She was about to put her phone down and continue watching the movie, but they ended up responding quicker than she had expected.

leehyuck:
anytime, princess

leehyuck:
say, that cafe you're in front of is that
one on the corner of 8th street, right?

kimhyeyeon:
oh, yeah, it is.

leehyuck:
isn't that a flower boy cafe?

kimhyeyeon:
maybe ._.

kimhyeyeon:
what's it to you?

leehyuck:
calm down, princess, I'm not judging.

leehyuck:
just usually the girls who go to those are desperate
whores, but something tells me you're quite the opposite

kimhyeyeon:
interesting assumption, mister lee donghyuck

leehyuck:
call me hyuck

leehyuck:
I'm sure it isn't one. no way a girl that stunning
is anything close to that.


Chapter sixteen; donghyuck

Monday had rolled around faster than she'd planned. Having had spent the entire Sunday doing absolutely nothing but laying around before going out with Cheng, it had been time well spent that had no doubt passed by in mach speed.

He'd even dropped her off at school that day, the entire ride he reminded her at least fifty times don't forget to ask Jaemin. The fact her best friend was suddenly playing some sort of matchmaker was almost terrifying to her, but whenever she'd ask he would only shrug and say, you're a lonely bitch.

Deciding to let it go, she hadn't even actually planned to ask him in the first place. She just - didn't trust him (or maybe she did and she's just lying to herself,) either way, Hye had a feeling in the back of her throat that Sicheng would find out if she really did or not. The realization that he was the type of best friend to dead-ass follow her to the party and check was very apparent in her cloud of thoughts, and she realized that she might as fucking well just do it. What did she really have to lose?

Although there was a nervous feeling she could feel rising up her throat through out that entire day. Distracting herself with other things, by the time it was lunch break, she was just thinking about how gorgeous that guy at the cafe was. I wonder how old he is, he definitely was out of highschool - but he couldn't be that old. Then there was the weird guy she'd started talking to Saturday after he dm'ed her. All she knew about him was his name and few random things, but nothing about his appearance or what school he went to. Although apparently he only a year older than her and lived in Chicago.

It was almost crazy to her to think about the unusual interaction she'd had recently. Is this what it feels like to have friends? she could almost think as she hiked her bag a bit further up her shoulder. Maybe she couldn't exactly qualify the stranger, Hyuck, or Jay from the cafe her friends but - she was anyway.

Her converse clicked against the tiled hallway of DMHS, the senior hallway where all of her class thrived. Completely used to the dirty looks and whispers that would spread through out the many groups of students that stood watching as she walked by, she felt different that day. Instead of sending back the usual witty comment and glaring right back at them, she smiled. It was something none of them had ever witnessed her doing was smiling, and they'd all immediately whispered even more to each other.

"do you see that? she's like a mental patient."

"hey, I heard Donghyuck commented on her Instagram post."

The sudden sound of someone speaking that name caused her to look to the people who had just said it. As she did this, her green eyes frantically searching for where such a sentence had come from, realizing that they'd just been talking about the stranger - the weird, oddly sweet, flirty stranger.

He went to DMHS?

Idiotically, she hadn't stopped walking forward through out the halls as she'd turned to search for who had said that. So he goes here? she thought in surprise. Perhaps he was even in her class and she just never noticed him, which almost made her feel bad.

If he did apparently attend DMHS, it sort of made her feel better. At least now she knew he wasn't a predator or some sort of pedophile, right?

Her eyes searched and searched, desperate to find these students that knew who he was, when the sudden feeling of someone running into her. Some sort of squeak, much like that of a dying rat, left her lips as she stumbled back a bit. Having would've fallen straight to her death, she - and the stranger that stood before her - managed to catch herself, her eyes widening as she hurriedly regained her composure to look up to who it was.

"might want to look ahead when you walk instead of sideways," his eyes peered into hers, the gaze he held over her feeling deadly. The brown within them seemed to mock her as she took a mere step back, clearing her throat, before even processing what it was he just said to her.


The gay queen, she realized exactly who it was, using the nickname she'd given to him a long time ago in her head. He was also the guy she'd met that night at Jisung's party, who said he hated Jisung despite him being part of his gang. She'd never made sense as to how the hell that even worked, and had never gotten to ask his name even, but now here he was - standing right before her.

Looking behind him for a moment, she noticed that just like he'd said, there was no sight of Jisung or any of his dogs.

"My bad, maybe you should've avoided walking into me, unless you were also not looking," she'd finally rose a brow in challenge to the boy before her.

His freshly tinted red locks (which he must've done this weekend) fell over his forehead in a perfect fringe, and the only facial piercing he had - a lip ring - seemed to shine under the light beaming down on them from the ceiling. This boy, whom she still didn't know the name of, seemed to glare at her for a moment. She could almost feel herself growing intimidated.

That was, until he broke out into a laugh. It was a bit sarcastic, pouring from his lips as his chocolate eyes brightened, and he hummed rather casually, "calm down, princess, it was only a joke."

Her eyes widened from the name that left his lips, but before she could say another thing, he'd walked right past her, heading somewhere down the hallway the complete opposite of where she was going. Feeling the eyes of literally everyone on her, they had all no doubt heard her conversation with him, and she could only await for whatever bullshit they'd make up to be spread. It was almost insane to think he would even talk to her in the first place, especially if it wasn't by Jisung's orders and to mess with her.

Guess he meant it when he said he really didn't listen to Jisung.

Shaking her head, she watched as he disappeared out the exit doors far on the other end of the hall. Through out this time, he didn't look back once. She couldn't deny his manner nor the way he walked, holding his head high in the air like he was some form of royalty. It was quite the sight.

"princess," she mumbled to herself, shaking her head before continuing on her way to lunch, "must be a common pet name."

The rest of the walk to the cafeteria had her pondering everything. She was thinking about so many people at once it was almost overwhelming. Trying to push the thoughts away, she'd pulled out her phone from her bag, hoping that Sicheng had texted her so she could either rant or clear her mind.

However, as the screen had lit up and the notifications began to load, she didn't see one from her best friend.

leehyuck:
your outfit today is nice

kimhyeyeon:
uhhh, thanks? but how do you know what
i'm wearing unless you're stalking me

leehyuck:
ew, don't insult me. I'm not a stalker,
princess, I don't have time for that.

leehyuck:
I saw you in the halls today, that's all

kimhyeyeon:

aha, so you DO go to dmhs?

leehyuck:
un-fucking-fortunately

leehyuck:
or maybe not so much now, since I get to
see you everyday !

kimhyeyeon:

wowza, you're smthn else, Hyuck

leehyuck:
thanks, I like to call myself a certified
genius:)

kimhyeyeon:

feel like that's a little far fetched

leehyuck:
oH please, you don't even know who I am

kimhyeyeon:

YEAH because I don't really pay attention to people,
and your crusty ass won't even accept my follow request

leehyuck:
she out here - calling me crusty.

leehyuck:
I'll accept it eventually. I just have so many
different requests to go through!! :(

kimhyeyeon:

what are you? a fucking celebrity?

leehyuck:
I mean, basically

kimhyeyeon:

ok, hyuck, then how come I don't know who tf you are?

leehyuck:
because, hye, your heads always in the clouds

leehyuck:
maybe you should pay more attention
to your surroundings, princess

Rolling her eyes, she could nearly feel herself growing frustrated by talking to Donghyuck. This guy, she shook her head in annoyance whilst stepping down the steps that led into the cafeteria. The last text he'd send about paying more attention to her surroundings seemed to repeat in her head multiple times, and this was the reason her eyes darted every which way, scanning over every person in the room.

With all the students that attended her school, how the hell was she supposed to gather which one he was?! it was complete fucking bullshit that she wasn't in the mood for as she turned off her phone, walking to sit somewhere empty in the corner, where she always sat.

It was when she'd thrown her bag onto the usual table you would always find her at, before actually looking up, did she notice the other person sitting at it. The sight of someone being there scared her almost, but she tried not to show that on her face as she took in his appearance.

The remembrance of the last events that had happened between them seemed to sink into her mind, and she cleared her throat, about to speak - when Jaemin beat her to it.

"hey, you're not still upset with me, are you?" there was a hopeful smile on his lips, and his eyes were bright as they bored into hers. How could you be upset with that? she wondered as his earrings dangled back and forth from his ears ever so slightly, his caramel hair styled to the side - reminding her of Jay's from the cafe - with a pastel pink sweat shirt over his shoulders.

She slowly sunk into the chair next to him, a long exhale leaving her lips, "nope, I'm not upset with you," she'd met his eyes again as she said this, only to see his grin growing wider from the sound of such words.

"Good, you had me worried," he'd hummed, setting his chin in the palm of his hand as he spoke, "I'm sorry for bringing up such a sore subject, I promise I won't ask unless you're comfortable telling me, alright?"

Aw, her heart could almost bleed in her chest. She had to break their eye contact so he didn't see how much his considerate words hurt her.

"Thanks, Nana," she finally said, returning the warm smile he always seemed to be giving her, "that means a lot."

He'd only kept smiling as he rose to his feet - did he ever stop?  Jaemin ruffled her hair as he informed, "I'm going to get food - for both of us - whether you like it or not. So be right back~!" he'd sing-songed the last part, and it almost sounded musical in a weird way. Before she could even process how he'd said both of them, Jaemin was walking away towards the lunch line.

fucker, she sighed, shaking her head as she looked back down to her phone. It was hard to believe she'd really come across someone like him.






She swore, sometimes she felt the urge to punch Sicheng in the nose - even though that's impossible for her to ever accomplish. It didn't mean she didn't still feel like it sometimes.

"I'm back," there he was, sing-songing those two words again like some sort of opera singer. She'd looked up to see Jaemin setting a tray of school lunch food in front of her, before he returned to his own seat with his tray right beside her.

A sigh left her lips as she peered down at the salad, fruit, and weird-ass rectangular pizza that the school served. Her heart no doubt ached at the kind gesture as she'd looked to him, "you really didn't have to get me lunch, you know."

He only shrugged, already eating his salad, "you shouldn't skip lunch, Yeonnie."

Pursing her lips, she tried to hide the grin that wanted to spread over them, and instead beginning to eat the food he'd bought for her. Ever since she was young, she'd despised school food with all of her might. At least as DMHS, it'd always been fucking horrible, which was mainly why she just never got lunch there. Of course, there was also because she didn't want to possibly be bothered by Jisung or anyone else. So, she'd always just sat, a loner in her corner.

That was, before Nana came along.

She'd sighed as they ate in silence except for the fact Nana would make small talk every so often. He was such a cheery, sweet person, who seemed to care so genuinely for her well being it was astonishing. It reminded her a bit of Sicheng, but he was just - different.

Although she told herself that she wouldn't, she found herself trusting Na Jaemin faster than she'd planned.

The Halloween party, she'd suddenly remembered what Sicheng had been bothering her about all the way until now from this weekend. Would it be good to ask him now or wait until last period? she wasn't sure, but there was a feeling that he might get asked by a trillion more girls if she kept waiting. It wasn't like that was a big issue to her or anything...

"Nana," she finally spoke his name, and the boy had looked up from eating his peaches to meet her glowing eyes. Just the sight of him peering back at her was enough to almost make her forget what she was about to even do, until she quickly cleared her throat, "are you going to the Halloween party?"

There was a look of confusion on his face for a moment. He'd diverted his eyes to the ceiling as he chewed the last of his fruit, swallowing it before that look of realization took over his features. "The one tomorrow night?" he'd asked in confirmation, and she'd only nodded rather hesitantly, "oh, I don't know, I wasn't going to. All these weird girls keep asking me so I was just gonna say I had something to do," he explained, before humming cheerily, "why do you ask?"

It's time to ask him, she could almost hear such a thought in her best friend's voice. Pushing a strand of dark hair behind her ear, she tried to find any words to speak in that moment, knowing it was the time to do what she'd been feeling bothered about all weekend. His words repeated in her head, all these weird girls keep asking me. I don't want to be one of those weird girls, she almost frowned as she stared down at her lap, trying to gather the courage she wasn't usually lacking this much.

"Yeonnie?" he'd said her nickname, looking at how she was staring at her lap in confusion.

Whipping her head up to look at him, she let out a small sigh before seeming to find the words hidden in the back of her throat, "I don't usually go, either, but I was thinking I would if you'd go with me?" she tried to say as clear as possible, but her voice pitch had highly increased due to how nervous she was.

Jaemin had only found this incredibly cute though as he found himself giggling at the way she spoke. His heart had seemed to explode into some sort of frenzy whilst he bit his lip in thought. She really just asked me, he processed this, not bothering to hide the grin that was stretched from ear to ear.

"uh - of course - it's not a big deal if you don't want to go, though," she coughed a bit, looking anywhere but at Jaemin. She had no idea if the grinning he was doing was because he was seemingly happy, or if it was because he was trying not to laugh at her. This was making her extremely self conscious as she cleared her throat, trying to ignore the fact her cheeks were heating up a shade of red.

"don't be silly," it felt like an entire century before he'd finally spoke despite it only being a few seconds, "I'd love to go with you."

Swallowing the lump in his throat, he was unable to understand the yelling that was coming from that exact area despite how hard he'd focus on it.

"Do you think this is funny?" the voice of Taeyong had rung through the air, and he had an uneasy feeling - especially if the leader was there.

"No, nothing is funny. Just put him down, dude!" it was the voice of a pleading Renjun. He hadn't heard the usually hard-headed drug dealer sound that desperate in a long time. Haechan only stood with his back against the brick wall, trying to figure out what he should do in this situation and how.

Knowing them, there was no doubt only Taeyong here. The others had to be around as well, they were just hiding. He knew this well enough, but he also knew they wouldn't shoot him if he stepped out there.

Or maybe he didn't know that, but he didn't care, either.

"How about I kill him right now? It seems like that's what it'll take for you kids to get it through your thick fucking skull that this territory doesn't belong to you."

The sound of a gun being cocked was heard only a second after his old leader had spoke these words, his tone dripping of wit. You could practically hear the smirk in his voice. Taeyong knew exactly what he was doing, he always had, and exactly how to do it. The only people he'd ever cared about were his own, so if you didn't happen to be that - he'd kill you without a second thought.

Which was why Haechan was confused as to why he hadn't shot whoever he was holding right then. It was most likely he wasn't done pushing their buttons, but either way he didn't want to test the waters by waiting any longer.

There was a long pause of silence as the brave boy had stepped out into the open. His hands were both at his sides, one of them cautiously raised over where he kept his weapon. All eyes had snapped to him the moment he stepped from the dark, only looking at Taeyong, who's eyes didn't look surprised at all.

"If it isn't Haechan," he'd chuckled at the sight, and Haechan saw then the one he was holding by the collar was no one other than Chenle. Typical. "Quite the gang you and Mark have built yourselves, huh?" he'd pushed the gun that was against Chenle's head further into his skull, his finger dangerously close to the trigger. The boy had winced under his grasp, obviously being terrified but not wanting to show it.

He'd looked back to the others who had somehow managed to get themselves into a mess they honestly deserved. There was a visible absence in Jisung and Mark, making it only Chenle, Jeno, and Renjun that were there. It was a sad sight, the fact the leader wasn't even there for his own fight. Even more of the reason he never deserved such a position,

Turning back to the platinum haired boy he once looked up to, a deep sigh left his lips, "trust me, it's not me or Mark's gang anymore."

He'd only rose a brow at his words, before questioning further, "Speaking of, where is little Mark anyway - still too scared to come out after pussying out all those years ago?" he knew exactly what he was trying to do as he spoke again, "it's a real shame you followed after him like some sort of lost puppy, now look where you've landed yourself. Working with a bunch of premature children," he snorted loudly by the end of his statement.

He's trying to anger me, he had to remind himself many times. This was part of Taeyong's game, and he was lucky he knew that.

"this motherfucker..." Jeno had been mumbling angrily as he cocked his own gun, an AK that was golden was in between his arms.

Before Haechan could tell him to stop whatever his plan was, he'd already raised the gun to aim it at his head. His finger just hovering over the trigger, he realized it was too late as his voice would have no effect anymore. Especially at the sight of his old gang members stepping out of the open, including one behind Jeno and Renjun.

"Watch out!" but it'd been no use when Sicheng had been the one behind them, who'd wrapped an arm around Jeno's neck, causing him to drop the gun. The red haired boy could only wince at the sight as he'd pulled his strength against his neck, not choking him enough to kill him, but only enough so he'd pass out.

Sicheng let the now unconscious body fall to the ground, picking up the gun he had previously about to of fired and now aiming it at Renjun. The others that were there were aiming it right at Haechan.

"What a brave soul," Taeyong bitterly laughed, finally letting go of his grip on Chenle. The boy weakly fell to the ground, before forcing himself off the ground where he backed up next to Haechan.

"Listen, we really don't want any trouble, guys," Haechan put his hands up in defense, realizing that even with him here they were outnumbered and out-skilled.

Taeyong only shrugged, "you should've listened the first time, then," he hummed, "since you're such an old friend, I'll give you one more fucking chance to never step foot here again, alright? If you do - I'm hanging all your fucking heads on platters, and anyone else you fucking care about."

Exhaling slowly, he quickly nodded, wanting nothing more than to get the hell out of there and make sure none of these idiots ever thought about coming back. He was honestly astonished they were even considering not killing them all on the spot and just being done with it. An act of mercy from Taeyong and the rest of 127 was more than rare.

"Alright, we won't sell here," he'd nodded again, before looking to Renjun, harshly speaking the words to send the message of what he was thinking, "Right, Renjun?!"

"uh, yes - you're right. I won't do business here, really!" it'd took him a moment to find his words, until Sicheng had pushed the gun he'd taken from Jeno's passed out corpse against his head.

"Good," Taeyong had grinned, turning swiftly to walk away. The others hadn't lowered their weapons as some of them followed, but a particular two stayed behind.

A long sigh left Haechan's lips as he closed his eyes for a split second, trying to regain his emotions after that. Something hadn't managed to nerve wreck him that badly in a long time, and he almost felt like he was going to pass out, himself.

Running a hand through his red locks, he had opened his brown orbs again to see two people standing before them that weren't either of his members as they were both tending to Jeno

"Sucks our first reunion since your parting went so poorly," Yuri had laughed at her own joke, still having her gun in her hand and no doubt loaded in case either Renjun or Chenle tried anything.

He didn't know quite what to say to the sudden friendly attitude he was receiving when they'd all been about to shoot his head off only a moment ago. Haechan guessed that it wasn't technically their doings, at least not mentally, but Taeyong's. His old leader obviously still had harsh feelings towards him and Mark for how they'd parted, and he guessed he couldn't blame him for that. The others were just following his orders.

"I know it wasn't your call to keep selling here since Jisung is so stupid but - I really would watch out for them trying to do it again," Sicheng had advised, "because it'll be bad. Taeyong isn't taking any shit right now because your friend there shot Kun."

His eyes widened at his words, but that wasn't the only thought that appeared in his head then. "Jeno shot Kun?" he realized, his eyes falling out of their sockets, now he was especially lost at why Taeyong didn't shoot them on sight. It made no sense, unless there's something else up their sleeves. But there was something else he was confused about, "how did you know Jisung's the leader?"

Haechan had heard a little about how Win and Jisung used to be friends and actually went to DMHS. But he didn't exactly know much about him in general, as he had just been joining back when he and Mark were with them. Not even that, he'd still been in trial, more like. So he was never well acquainted with him.

He'd only hummed, not that bothered by his question, "I have a friend connected to him."

Thinking about this hard for a minute, he'd tuned everything out due to the fact his thoughts spoke much louder. Haechan didn't actually know his real name, much like he didn't know his. But as he thought about just who he would possibly know that's connected to Jisung somehow and not in the gang - there was a small suspicion that rose in his brain.

"Does that connection happen to be female?" he rose a brow in question. At the sound of these words, Win's eyes widened a bit, clearly not expecting him to ask such a thing.

Yuri had been listening in to whatever was happening, and gasped loudly, seeing the expression of her fellow member, "what - Win actually talks to girls?!"

He glared at her before looking back to him, "what's it to you?"

It has to be her, it was the only thing that made sense. Who else did Jisung know that would have that kind of information? No one.

"Does Hyeyeon know you're involved in these sorts of things?" he'd crossed his arms over his chest, thinking of the fragile girl that was sitting in his BMW as they spoke, "Is she aware you openly murder people in cold blood?"

WinWin hadn't expected him to actually know her name, and Yuri hadn't known what to say much like him from such questions being asked.

"It's not like she'll believe whatever you tell her, she hates you and the rest of Jisung's fucking fiends," he'd rolled his eyes, clearly thinking it wasn't a big deal.

But Haechan had only smirked, "funny, I can go tell her right now, we'll see how that'll turn out."

Win had only furrowed his brows, "You say that like you're actually friends or some-," his words were cut off by someone yelling from ahead of Haechan at the end of the alleyway.

"GUYS, TAEYONG SAID TO COME THE FUCK ON OR HE'S GOING TO SLAUGHTER BOTH OF YOU!"

Johnny's voice rung through their ears, and Yuri immediately started heading the way they'd come after bidding goodbye to Haechan. Win sighed as he glanced back to his two members, before reluctantly looking back to the red haired boy before him, "If you tell her anything, I'll come kill you myself," was all he'd snapped, his eyes burning holes into Haechan's soul before he'd swiftly turned and left just like that.

Haechan could only watch as his body disappeared down the alley, before turning back to his friends that were still sitting by Jeno.

He opened his mouth to tell them they needed to get the hell home, but Chenle had spoken up before he had a chance, "you're friends with Hyeyeon?"

Rolling his eyes, he decided it wasn't worth his time to even speak to them. "Is that really what you're worried about now?" a sigh of disappointment left his lips before he shook his head, already walking away down the way he came as he announced, "I'm leaving."



Chapter twenty one; the truth untold

Humming along to Bang x3 that played softly from the speakers of Haechan's BMW that she'd grown rather accustomed to (it's her dream car,) she'd been sitting like that, leaned back in the leather seat, and staring at the ceiling for what had most likely been an hour and a half if not more. She'd heard multiple gun shots towards the first thirty minutes or so, but finally they'd stopped. In worry, she found herself wondering if anyone had got shot - whoever may be there - especially Haechan, which is honestly the only one she cared about.

It was when her phone finally dinged after practically the entire day that she sat up. Her green eyes lit up at the sight of Sicheng finally texting her after so long, but the words which she read aloud to herself weren't ones she'd expected from him.

despite how she had been terrified of the area they were in, something inside of her was feeling mighty. When she didn't get a reply from him after waiting, she knew exactly what she was going to do.

Find out for herself.

Sicheng might think she had no idea, and that he might really have her fooled - but if he'd been lying to her after this time, she only had another reason as to why she never trusted anyone. Already knowing it had to be true because it was the only thing that would make any sense, she still wanted to know - to see it for herself. She wanted to see him in person, and the look in his eyes when he realizes he's been caught.

Taking the keys out of Haechan's shining red BMW, she shoved them in the pocket of her hoodie before climbing out of the vehicle. The chilling, cold air immediately pricked at her skin when she'd locked the car, the eery night seeming to speak to her.

It's fine, she told the side of her brain that was freaking out over her getting out of the car in a place like this, there's not even anyone around here. I have to see if it's really true, is what Hyeyeon endlessly reminded herself. Her heart was already aching from the thought her best friend had really been lying to her - about something she just wasn't sure about yet.

To think he was the one who kept telling her to stay away from illegal things.

Her converse clicked against the road as she ran across it. The street lights flickered from how old they were, and she stopped right in front of the dark alleyway she'd witnessed Haechan go into only a couple hours ago.

Am I really going to go in there? she asked herself, still feeling a bit afraid. Never was she someone who was easily scared by things, but a situation like this was a completely different story. The area she was at was the bad, dead side of Chicago, where gangs thrived and violence lived higher than any other area.

The South side was the area her parents had worked on keeping her from her entire life. Now that she was in it, she wasn't sure how to act other than tremble at the sight.

Reminding herself of the mission, she'd only stepped one foot onto the gravel path of the alley when rustling was heard from somewhere behind her.

Her ears perking up, her entire body grew stiff at the sound. It had been footsteps, she knew this well, as her entire body quickly turned around towards wherever it had come from. Being a bit into the alley now as she backed up cautiously, trying to calm the nerves that were on fire with in her frail figure, she was unable to see where this person was hiding from the narrow view she had towards the outside.

This can't be happening, she prayed that it was just Haechan, or even one of Jisung's gang members. She just hoped it was someone that wasn't going to kill her or something else.

Continuing to back up, she decided her best bet was going the way she saw Haechan go. After all, he was the only protection she knew of that had to be somewhere close by.

As her shoes cracked against the gravel, she kept a close eye on the entrance where the noise had come from. Only then was it that she witnessed a man come jump out from one of the sides, wearing all black from head to toe and a mask that covered his entire body. He was much bigger than her due to how tiny she was in general, and her eyes had bulged out of their sockets at the sight of him.

He didn't say a word, and she tried not to freeze - until he'd broke into a run after her.

Oh my god, the three words repeated in her head as she broke into a run right after. Her heart beat was out of her chest at that point, tears brimming her eyes from how terrified she was. Her life felt like a horror movie, and she absolutely hated it.

Her thoughts were so loud that she didn't hear whatever the man was yelling to her as he chased her. Tears spilled from her eyes as she ran for what seemed like her life, unable to hold back the fear that was evident inside of her.

She'd turned down another alleyway into what she hoped she'd find Haechan, running and running with every ounce of strength she had. But she could hear him growing closer to her, and it was making her feel helpless. He's faster than me.

It was when the alley she'd turned down ended up being a dead end that she realized it was really over. She was finally experiencing everything her parents tried to keep her from.

"How unfortunate for you," the man's voice was deep, and from his posture she could tell he was a lot older and not anyone she knew. Her back hit the brick wall of the dead end, her entire body shaking with fear as he stepped closer and closer to her.

Finally, he was standing right before her, his height towering over hers much like every other person she knew. His hands raised to grab her cheeks, and he'd chuckled to himself, "what's a girl like you doing out on this side of town?" he'd hummed more to himself than her as his grip on her cheeks went down to her jaw, where he'd forced her to turn her head on either side, as if he was examining her features.

Her hands went up to grab his wrists, trying to push him off of her. This ended up being no use since her strength was so little, and she found herself angrily struggling to even speak from how hard his grip was, "I swear to god - if you don't let me go right now."

Knowing her threat was rather empty, he'd laughed at it, "oh, you'll do what?"

She'd had something up her sleeve indeed, some form of a last attempt at calling anyone - but hopefully Haechan. Her lips had parted as she let out an ear-piercing, deafening scream. The sound seemed to bounce off the brick walls of the dark, narrow alley, traveling through the night. It'd even hurt the mans ears as he winced from such a thing.

"What the hell are you trying to pull?!" his voice was angered, much like his flaming eyes.

His grip had then went to her neck, her eyes widening as he began to tighten it. Coughing from the air that was now growing lengthy from how it kept getting tighter and tighter, she asked herself then if it was really the end of her rather short lived life.

Struggling, she continued to try to pry his hands off of her with her own. It was then she wished she'd lifted weights or something to at least give herself a chance, but it was no use.

So, seeming to lose faith, she'd squeezed her eyes shut as her entire body felt as if it was shutting down. Everything was happening slowly but surely, and that was what she expected to be one of the last things she'd think as she tuned out whatever the man was trying to say to her.

The sound of a gunshot had suddenly shot through the air, and if she thought everything had once been happening slowly - it was now in fast motion. A scream left her lips from how loud the sound of the weapon had been, and she felt the circulation coming back to her as blood had began to pour through the man that had been about to kill her's head where the bullet had clearly gone through. His eyes rolled back in his head as he collapsed to the ground, the red substance pouring from his body at an irregular pace and forming a puddle under his corpse.

She'd just witnessed someone die, it took her a while to process as her entire body began to shake. Her green eyes couldn't seem to tear away from his dead body, and it was difficult for her to really process what had happened.

"Hey," she heard a soft, honey like voice that at first, she didn't even recognize, "fuck, are you okay?"

Haechan was standing right before her, his shoes getting stained by the blood puddle. His eyes were peering down at her from his height, and she hadn't even realized the tears that were pouring from her emerald eyes as she managed to look up to him.

At the sight of her crying, he let out a slow exhale, "I told you not to get out of the car, it's dangerous for you here," Haechan had only mumbled. He wasn't quite sure what to do after such an event. Here she was, crying before him, a girl which he felt like he didn't know well enough but at the same time close to.

Hesitantly, he stepped forward to enclose the space between them, wrapping his arms around her. Her body was stiff as she cried harder, before relaxing into him. Slowly, he'd felt her small arms find their way around his waist, and the fragile girl whom he'd just saved buried her face into his velvet jacket.

There was a long silence other than the sound of him shushing her gently as boy awkwardly allowed her to sob in his chest. Haechan couldn't blame her for what she was feeling. She'd probably never been in a place like this despite her seemingly fearless attitude. He knew she hadn't expected something like that to happen, but the South side was a dangerous place.

Although it looked dead and shut down, it was where violence thrived. Many gangs even he didn't know about were most likely hidden in the shadows of the cramped downtown that had long been abandoned by the normal townsfolk, hiding low in the territory so they didn't face the wrath of 127. Rarely did these said people ever come out, but he guessed one of them had saw the lone, frail girl walking by herself and had sickly jumped at the chance.

He didn't know what that guy had been planning, and as he looked down to his dead, old body, he didn't recognize him either. For all he knew, he could've been one of the people Renjun was selling to.

Either way, he didn't care. The only thing he knew he had to do then was get her home.

"Come on," his voice was a soft whisper as he disconnected their hug, beginning to walk away. When he heard her not make a sound of movement, Haechan turned back to see she was still frozen, her body trembling like she was stuck in a time lapse. He frowned at how she seemed so petrified, it hadn't been what he wanted at all. why the hell did she get out of the car?

Stepping back towards her, he wasn't sure what else to do as he grabbed her hand. Hyeyeon had jumped at the sudden contact, finally being able to divert her eyes from the body to look up at him instead. He took that as the time to speak, "let's get you home, okay?"

She coughed a bit as if to rid the tears away that wouldn't stop falling, hurriedly stepping over the dead body of the man. Don't look back, she repeatedly told herself, not wanting to see such a sight again. The only thing she would let herself focus on was the feeling of Haechan's hand in hers, and the fact he seemed to be one of the only people she some what felt safe with. After realizing how Sicheng had lied to her about what he seemed to be involved in, she felt glad to know Haechan. At least he's honest about being involved in a gang.



Chapter twenty two; comfort

"Try not to think about it, alright? It's really not as big of a deal as your mind is making it out to be," Haechan had been assuring her, parking his BMW against the curb in front of her home, "it was just some old creep, it would've come to him eventually - and he fucking deserved it," he mumbled the last part angrily, gripping the steering wheel before putting the vehicle in park.

The brunette didn't seem to have any words to say. She hadn't had any for the longest time. All she could think about was how her best friend had been lying to her, and how she was idiotic for thinking he just altered his appearance to fit in with his new school. To make the entire day worse, after witnessing Jisung fight Jaemin, ending up with the both of them probably being suspended - she'd witnessed Haechan shoot someone.

It'd been too long of a day for her to process, and she tangled her fingers in her hair, trying to forget it all.

Jaemin, she remembered the boy she'd grown so close to. He was one of the only normal people she knew - or practically the only one - with Sicheng being crossed off the list. She wished she had his number, that she could talk to him. After all this, she trusted him, and she desperately needed someone to vent to then.

"I-I know," she finally replied to Haechan's previous words after sitting in silence for a moment, "I was just - in shock - not only from that but from everything that's happened today."

The red haired boy had turned in his seat to fully face her before he'd hummed the question, "Like what? The whole Jaemin and Jisung thing?" he spoke casually, but on the inside Haechan was highly debating with himself. A part of him wanted to tell her about Sicheng and how he was lying to her. If they were such great friends, she didn't deserve to be in the dark about what kind of person he really was. But something was holding him back from doing so.

She'd shrugged at the question, "I guess - I just don't get what Jisung's deal is. It's weird because just this morning I asked Jaemin to the Halloween party - and then next thing I know, Jisung is starting a fight with him," she vented only a portion of the worries on her mind, "I can't help but feel like it's my fault - but I just don't understand why he does this."

He'd watched her pained expression carefully, and there was a small feeling forming inside of him he didn't notice then. Clearing his throat, he looked up at the ceiling in thought for a moment, "well, princess, the reason Jisung started a fight with Jaemin was because of the drugs he put in his drink that night, I'm sure you know. He had Renjun slip a dose of DXM into his drink, and now he's claiming Jaemin asked for it and owes him money for it," looks like he's back to the name calling, "he was saying that he had to pay up today, but Jaemin seems to know it was a set up so he's refusing - and probably doesn't have that kind of money, either."

Surprised at the full story she hadn't completely figured out but now knew, she could only gawk. "How much money is he asking him for?" He really didn't tell me any of this, she was partly hurt even though it was most likely because Jaemin didn't want her to get involved. The thing he failed to understand was that she already was involved, she always had been if it had to do with Park Jisung.

He looked rather hesitant to tell her as he broke their eye contact. Haechan's vision looked behind her towards the house she lived in, his eyes widening as he saw how large it really was. He should've known earlier her family was definitely one of the wealthy types in Chicago when she'd told him it was on this side. Although one thing he noticed was the entire house almost looked abandoned. With Halloween literally being tomorrow, even the guys house had some decorations (Mark's idea) and at least there were cars usually parked in the drive way.

But her home - looked dead. Not a singular car was parked, and he wondered where her parents where. They have to still be connected to her, he'd thought, she can't be an orphan like myself and live in a house like that.

As he realized how much cash this girl might have up her sleeve, he didn't feel guilty about telling her, "A thousand."

Her once worried expression turned one of relief as soon as the amount left his lips, "oh, that's - that's not horrible like I was expecting."

Haechan only shrugged, "yeah, but Jaemin doesn't seem to have access to money like that."

Pursing her lips, she felt a bit better at what she was going to do, being able to make a small, close lipped smile despite the events of that day, "oh, I think I know what I'll do to fix this." He'd about to of asked her what he probably already knew, but she'd opened the car door, climbing out with her Halloween costume bag in hand.

Watching her climb out of his car, he'd decided that'd been enough conversation for the night, anyway. After the day they'd both had, this girl needed rest. He had a good feeling that she was still rather shaken up from everything and was just putting on an act.

"Alright, I'll see you tomorrow, then," he'd offered her a small grin as she was peeking her head through the opened car door.

"Thank you for everything, Haechannie, really," her smile looked genuine that time, her green eyes twinkling under the large street lights above them, "I'm glad I met you."

Her last statement caught him at surprise. It was something he hadn't heard from anyone in a long time, and hearing this girl he'd only known for a short time speak such words had him in awe - which he quickly hid before it could show on his facial expression.

"you're welcome, princess."

She'd stepped back, closing the door to the red BMW she'd grown to love after spending all day in it. Hyeyeon waved at him as he was already driving away, feeling a bit sad when he didn't return it.

That was, until she noticed the bright smile that spread across his lips. It was enough to make her feel content, even for a small second, with her new friend.

Fumbling with the house keys that were inside her pocket with her phone, she pulled them out of her hoodie. The moon and street lights being her only source of visibility in the night, she bent down to unlock the front door of her home. After such a day, Hyeyeon was more than ready to pass out on her couch.

Closing and locking the door behind her, she'd kicked off her sneakers to the side. Walking into the living room and setting down the bag that contained her costume, she'd fell back onto the couch as a long yawn left her lips.

"Finally home," she mumbled to herself at the euphoric feeling of safety.

Already feeling sleep begging for her to allow it to take over her, she was just about to, when her phone vibrated.

It was then she realized she hadn't checked it at all ever since she sent those last texts to Sicheng, before she'd gotten out of the car earlier. Rubbing her eyes as she sat up, pulling the device out of her hoodie pocket and turning on the screen.







Exhaling, she exited out of the conversation. There were too many questions she had to ask him that she wanted to know the answers to, but was also afraid. Hyeyeon knew that with everything that had happened today, she couldn't take anymore things that would put more thoughts into her head.

After regaining herself, she'd looked back down to her phone screen. It was still open on iMessage, viewing at the text conversations she had. At the top of the screen, from where her phone had went off a moment ago, was a new conversation with a number she didn't have in her phone.

Staring down at it for a moment, she'd completely forgotten about how she'd saw Jay today at the cafe.

After closing out of the conversation, she changed his contact name. I'll have to remember to take a photo of him for his contact next time I see him, she reminded herself.

Turning on some music to fall asleep to, the sound of Muse filled her ears as she laid back into the soft plush of the sofa. It was the exact same spot Nana had passed out in that night, and she chuckled to herself at the memory, grabbing the same blanket she had covered him with off the back of the couch. Pulling it over her, she'd been too tired to go upstairs to her room as sleep overcame her entire body.

She fell asleep to not the thought of Nana fighting Jisung, or the worry if he was okay. It wasn't the thought that he might not even show up to the party tomorrow thanks to the events of today, either. But it was the thought of his warm, welcoming smile that seemed to pull you in. The sound of his laugh when he'd joke around with you or you'd say something silly. She could hear the way he'd always sing song Yeonnie in the back of her head.

It took Hyeyeon a long time to find her father's old check book in his office. The entire room was dirty and dusty from no one ever being in it anymore. The walls where outlined with shelves, filled with many books she never cared to look at. Money didn't make up for their absence that was growing larger and larger in her life with the days that passed.

Shaking her head, she pushed the thoughts away and forced herself to focus on the current situation. She hadn't even heard from either of them in so long, she could almost cry at the thought despite how she refused to cry (but always ended up doing it anyway.)

Na Jaemin, she wrote, before it was at the amount. Thinking hard on it for a second, she'd shrugged, before scribbling down a larger number than he even needed.

She was writing Jaemin this check not even expecting him to be at school today, but hopefully he'd be at the party later. That was the small amount of hope she held onto as she'd made her way to school that morning, all the whilst distracting herself by texting Jay.

She ignored him due to the screaming going on inside her brain. Turning in her seat, her green eyes whip every which way, because she knew what kind of stare it was that she was receiving. She knew why it bothered her so much. It was the same feeling she'd felt before that man had chased her, only last night with Haechan.

Such a traumatizing night, one that she had forced to the very back of her brain. She'd witnessed a man die, and Hye hadn't thought she would have to face anything else to do with that matter. As Haechan said, don't worry about it, it ended.

So why did she have that petrifying feeling crawling up her spine?

No matter how hard she squinted, her eyes didn't find where it was coming from. Hye could feel her body growing tenser by the second, but as she looked and looked, the green irises fell on something else.

Si Cheng, she stared at the silhouette of his walking body. Hye wasn't focused on the ridiculous costume he sported, but more at the fact he really showed up. Despite the fact he'd said he was going to, she didn't really expect him, not after everything.

The only way to get past this conversation is by lightening the mood, she tells herself, forcing a smile onto her face, "that's pretty rude, you know."

Jaemin rolls his eyes at how she'd taken his caring words the wrong way, adjusting the white fedora-like hat upon his perfectly styled hair. "Oh shut up, we all know you're gorgeous."

His words were unexpected, and it became even harder for her to hide the shock in her expression. Hadn't Jaemin called her cute before? why did his sudden words have such an unusual effect on her? she figured it was just due to the fact her entire body was so shaken up, now everything was bothering her for absolutely no reason.

Sighing, she shakes her head at him, reaching out her pointer finger to poke his nose. "Cute of you to say, Na Jaemin."

He wrinkles his nose the moment she'd touched it, and the way he grinned down at her from his height was no doubt irresistible to any girl that wasn't Hyeyeon, "I prefer Nana."

She tries to recognize the voice, feeling the sudden presence of someone beside her. Her hands are tangled in her brunette locks, whimpers leaving her lips as she grips it in pain.

"Hey, hey," the voice is soft, and she feels arms wrapping around her, forcing her up, "you're fine, alright? I've got you."

Her body growing weaker by the second, the only thing she could think but not say due to lack of energy was the mere words, I hope so.

Chapter twenty six; indignation

His fist that wasn't holding up the boy clenched at his side. Without another thought, he pulled it back, before colliding it with Jisung's face. There was the sound of skin hitting skin, followed by a sharp crack, indicating it had most definitely hurt.

Chapter twenty seven; ptsd

Through out this time, her emerald eyes had been closed, ragged breathes leaving her lips as if she was trapped in some sort of horrid nightmare, unable to wake up.

Setting her on the soft mattress, pushed her hair that was falling in her face as her body unconsciously snuggled into the many pillows he had on his bed. His eyes stared down at her for a long while, and he felt a mix of emotions crowding within his body, more specifically his heart.

He wasn't sure how he felt. Sure, she'd ended up bailing on him for the whole 'ride to the party.' Anything like a text would've been nice, but he knew she didn't have his number, and had no idea that was his Instagram.
