Haechan lets out a sigh as he drives down the gravel road at a rather quick pace. It was actually rather intelligent for 127 to relocate to such an area, otherwise literally the middle of nowhere. He understood the motive, they were smart.

It sucked that their location was now compromised, however. But as far as he knew, so was theirs.

Pursing his lips as he drives, his eyes fixated on the small amount of the road he could actually see thanks to his head lights. The sky only got darker as you got further away from the city, and out in the country it felt dead, especially with the way the rain was screaming onto his windows.

Music is playing softly from the speakers, and like any other time, it still managed to be his medicine. One thing Haechan had always found peace in was just that - music. No matter what he was going through, just turning on the radio could seem to clear his mind, if even for a split second.

So throughout everything that had been going on that weekend, and what he was planning to do one he saw her, he found a way to hum along to the song that played through his car's stereo. The thought that was giving him happiness then, was the thought he could see her soon.

Finally, the mansion had come into view after driving down the road for what felt like a millennia. His eyes squint through the darkness as he turns right to pull into the driveway. Unlike earlier, there weren't any cars.

But as he peers out his window, he sees the door was wide open.

It left a bad feeling in his stomach.

Only then did his eyes land on a vehicle, indeed. It was some sort of pitch black van, that had once been camouflage in the dark until his eyes had adjusted to it well enough.

That's when he saw her.

"No - fucking - way," his words were a whisper as he shuffled in his seat, undoing the seatbelt and hurriedly opening the middle compartment to grab his gun.

It was unlike him to pull risky plays like this. After all, he had no idea if the guy was also armed, but what he did know was that the girl he had was Hyeyeon.

And he wasn't about to break another promise.

The millisecond he'd opened the door a gunshot had rung through the air - but it hadn't been from him. Haechan cursed as he ducked just beneath his car door, he knew that bullet would've hit otherwise.

Guess this answered the question as to if they're armed.

Anger welled up in his veins at just the thought of what was happening. These are them, he processed, these are the people who are after her. He was damn tired of the trouble they were adding onto their lives, he already had enough on his plate without whoever these people were adding onto it.

Every few seconds, he'd duck out to fire a shot towards the direction of the guy. But Haechan had to be careful not to hit Hyeyeon, which meant that his shots weren't very likely to hit anyone at all due to how worried he was it would.

A sigh leaves his lips as he tries to think of what to do. Right now, his car was still on, providing the guy the light to even see him in the first place. However, if he turned it off and distinguished that advantage, he could surprise him.

With this thought in mind, Haechan acted quickly to duck inside his car, pulling the keys out of the ignition and watching the lights go out.

This left the general area in darkness, but he had clear view of where the guy was. Slowly, he makes his way around the back of his car, keeping low in case the guy still had any vision. It wasn't difficult to make his way towards them, as the unknown man had called out into the darkness, "who are you? Come out now, and she won't get hurt."

He didn't know what the man was planning until he grew close enough to see - to see a gun aimed at her head.

Despite this, somehow, Hyeyeon was still trying to get out of his grasp. "I don't know who the fuck you people are, but I don't have anything you want!" she cries in annoyance, squirming around to get away from the feeling of a gun against her head.

He could tell she was trying to be strong, but deep down, she was a child.

"And I think you're wrong," the guy had bitterly laughed as if he was absolutely hilarious. It was enough to make Haechan want to kill him even more if that was possible, "how about you tell your friend to come out before I cast a bullet through your head, Hyeyeon?"

At these words, the girl had trembled. She was trying so hard not to show her fear, but at the sound of such a thing being said, she couldn't help it.

With that, she calls out into the darkness, "uh, Cheng - is it you?"

A snort was heard, "I don't think that's what I told you to say," he'd said in disappointment, before there was a sharp sound of something being hit. Haechan didn't know what it was until he'd heard a high pitched screech of pain echo through the air.

He could hear her cursing under her breathe until she'd cried, "you motherfucker - I swear to god if I ever find out who you are I'm going to personally-," another scream echoes through the air.

Unable to listen to it anymore, he stepped out into the open - directly behind the guy holding her. His gun clenches tightly beneath his grasp, and it was aimed right at his head.

"State your name and why you're here for her, and I'll consider sparing your life."

At the sound of the unexpected voice, Hyeyeon felt her heart clench in her chest, "Haechan?!"

But he wasn't interested in giving her a greeting then, it was time for business.

There's no reply from the boy who looked around their age, he only let her go, and weakly, she'd fell to the ground, cursing from the pain she was in. He only held the gun tighter against the mans head, preparing himself to pull the trigger that his finger fluttered over if he even looked like he was going to try something.

"I said, who are you and why are you here?!" he felt the need to repeat again, this time his voice came out deeper and much, much louder.

There isn't a reply, still, from the man. Instead, a abrupt, creepy laugh had erupted from his lips. It boomed through the previously tense air like flowers, sending chills down Hyeyeon's spine as she still was unable to see anything due to the blindfold. What was going on? How was Haechan even here? it felt like she was dreaming from how weird and confusing it all was.

Out of complete anger, Haechan had broke. It was like everything had come pouring out of him at once as he grabs the guy's shirt from the back, pulling him back until he hit the back of the van he had been driving with a thud. Once he meets his eyes, which were so empty despite the fact he was greeting death, it had only made him angrier at his lack of response.

Haechan raises his fist, about to give him a taste of what he'd call pre death, when he'd finally opened his mouth, "you really think this is going to do anything? You have no idea what you're up against."

He narrows his eyes, "what the fuck are you talking about?"

"They're coming, they're coming for her no matter what you do," he'd spit out the words like venom, laughing in disbelief every few seconds like some sort of crazed lunatic, "and if you try to stop them, they'll come for you, too. They'll kill you, they'll kill you all, one by one."

He'd been staring at the man in confusion, "who? who is they?!" Haechan's demands, having only been holding him down with one hand against the van. This meant he didn't notice the fact the guy had the other hand free, the other hand with the weapon.

But he wasn't interested in shooting Haechan. He'd aimed the gun right at his head, and just as the boy noticed, screaming the word stop! It'd been too late.

Whoever he was, he'd shot a bullet right through his own skull. A gasp had left Hyeyeon's lips as she was still in a ball on the ground, and hadn't saw anything of what happened, but she knew that it had obviously not been good.

Haechan let's go of the guy, watching his now dead body fall to the ground in disbelief. The only words he could think were what the fuck, as he stares down at it for a while. The words repeat in his head over and over, almost sending him into some sort of trance.

"H-Haechan?"

He's snapped out of it at the sound of her voice, immediately turning to see she was still there. In a whisper, she calls out, "please tell me it wasn't you, I don't know what I'd do."

She sounded so torn, and in an instant he rushed to her side. Slowly, his hands reach out to grab her, pulling her up. Hyeyeon sniffles as he does so, "it's okay, princess, I'm here," his honey like voice calmed her everlasting nerves, dripping through her ears and creating a final feeling of safety she'd been missing.

Pulling the blind fold off of her eyes, he uses a pocket knife to cut off the ropes around her hands. Not even a second had passed when she practically jumped forward to wrap her arms around his neck, almost silent sobs leaving her lips as she buried her face in his jacket.

The rain was still pouring down, and had been through out this entire time. It was the entire reason he had been able to get behind the guy without him hearing him, after all.

The two of them sat there for a while, getting soaked from the weather. Haechan, for once, didn't have any words to say. He only wrapped his arms around the girl who was sobbing on his lap, rubbing her back comfortingly.

He didn't know what was going on. It didn't seem like whoever these people were, were after her for her involvement with gangs. It was something deeper.

"Hye, it's okay, you're okay," his voice was so soft, and her arms fell from around his neck so she could grab his shirt instead, bunching it up in her fists.

"Haechan, Donghyuck, I don't know what to call you," she whispers as she sits up so she's able to meet his eyes. The brown irises peer back at her, and he reaches a hand up to wipe away the tears, watching as the rain had soaked her hair.

"Donghyuck," he says after a while, "call me Donghyuck."

He hadn't let her speak due to how worried he was about her. "Are you hurt? Can you walk?" he began to bombard the poor girl with questions, taking the jacket off from around his shoulders and placing it over hers instead.

This jacket, she'd inhaled the scent of him as she grabbed onto the sleeves to pull it securely around her, only mumbling in reply, "I'm okay, really," but he'd still insisted on helping her up as the two of them rose to their feet. She loved this jacket, it was the same one he'd wore that day they met, and when they ran into each other the next morning.

"Okay," he nods in confirmation, but still grabs her hand as they make their way towards the car.

As the red BMW comes into view, and she tries to erase everything that had happened recently from her mind, there was still something that remained.

"Donghyuck, wait," she used the name, his real name, for the first time then. Haechan had been walking in front of her, still keeping a tight grip on her hand, but slowly turns at the sound of his name after a moment, he really wasn't used to hearing it anymore, not for years. But he liked the way it came off her tongue.

"Yeah, you okay?" he hums as he turns towards her.

The rain still pouring onto the both of them, Hyeyeon had no intention of saying any words. Just then, as she stared up at him through the darkness of that November night, with the droplets having had made his hair a wet mess atop his head, his white tee being soaked as well made his toned skin clearly visible through the fabric. And with the way his lips were there, so seemingly soft, with his brown irises peering down at her with that same look in them she never could understand - until now.

All of these things are what motivated her to step a singular step forward, going on her tip toes. Hyeyeon's hand reaches out to ball his soaked tee into her hand, pulling the boy forward so she could finally do what in reality - she'd been wanting to for longer than she knew.

She kissed him.

Chapter thirty five; bashful

"See you at school, Donghyuck," her voice was a mere whisper as she had hurriedly climbed out of the red BMW. The rain was beginning to calm down after the long, dead quiet drive back to her home, and Hyeyeon hadn't intended to say anything other than those five words. There were still droplets of water that fell atop her head as she hadn't even stopped to think about the fact she still had his jacket over her shoulders with how eager she was to get inside.

Everything had been too much for her. She didn't know what sort of overwhelming emotion had come over her suddenly. But she wasn't going to let it continue. Hyeyeon was scared, she was scared of the people after her and how determined they were. And she was scared of being with someone again after Jisung. It was why she wasn't going to let it go any further, at least that's what she told herself.

The grass crunches under her converse as she rushes through the grass. Her body had ached with each step, as she actually was in pain, but back there, she didn't want to tell Haechan just so he wouldn't worry anymore.

It was when she was already on her porch that she heard the sound of a car clicking, indicating it was now locked. Her green eyes go from having been looking down at her house keys in the lock of the door, to where Haechan was walking across her yard like she just had.

In a panic from how much she was afraid to speak to him right now after her actions, she hurriedly tried to unlock the door. It'd been a blessing when the heard the click of it being unlocked, but just as her small hand gripped the knob, someone had grabbed her wrist.

"Hye," his voice calls out to her, his grip not being tight enough to hurt, but yet tight enough so she was unable to get away, "I'm not going to let you be by yourself."

Swallowing the lump in her throat, she racks her brain for the right words to say. Still, she refused to turn and meet his eyes, she was scared to. Everything in the air felt awkward to her, she didn't know exactly what was going on in his complicated mind, and that terrified her. All she wanted to do was be by herself, even though deep down she knew it was dangerous.

She was too childish, which is the reason the first thing she thought to blurt out was, "I won't be, I can call Jaemin."

A part of her had hoped those words would be enough to get him to back off, to leave her be for the time being. When there was no sound coming from the boy for a second, she thought it worked.

That was, until the bright sound of his little chuckle had filled her ears. She scoffed silently in disbelief, her face still being out of his view. How does he find that funny?!

After a moment of laughing to himself, Haechan sighs in disappointment, "princess, he wouldn't be able to protect you from anything more than a fly."

His comment had been rude, but the insult towards her friend wasn't what she was focused on now. If anything, she was frustrated. Hyeyeon was frustrated with how witty, sarcastic, but fucking irresistible Haechan was. It made her want to do many things, but the current top one on the list was slamming her head into the door.

"Haechan," his original name comes out as a whisper, "please just let me be."

But she should've realized a long time ago how stubborn he was. "No," his voice had been rather demanding and stern at first, but as a few seconds passed, he seemed to be in deep thought over something. Only a moment later, Haechan had deeply exhaled, his voice coming out in a calmer tone as he spoke, "Hye, can you please talk to me instead of pushing me away? This isn't going to make anything better for you, I'm here, and I'm not going anywhere."

Something about what he said - or perhaps everything - had struck a soft spot in her heart. There's a long silence, and Hyeyeon peers ahead into her opened house door, staring into the dimly lit room that was once lively but now always felt so alone. After a second, a sigh leaves her lips, and she tries to walk forward into the house, only to be held back by him.

"Stupid, I'm trying to drag you inside," she still hadn't turned to look at him, and when she walked forward that time, he'd followed.

Haechan's hand had slid from her wrist into her own hand, where he tightly held so she wouldn't run away when he least expected it. Closing and locking the door behind them, Hyeyeon was dead silent once again as they stood inside her home.

Not knowing what else he could do, the red haired boy only waits.

"Haechan, listen," she has to clear her throat a few times, "I think you're great - really great - but I'm just - I'm really scared," her voice had cracked by the time she finished saying these things. It took him longer than usual to realize, but as he watched the way she hid her face by looking the opposite direction, he realized just why she was doing that.

"Hey," he calls out to her, but she'd cut him off by speaking again.

"I don't know who these people are, I don't know anything of what it going on, and people keep dying in front of me. There's so much death and violence everywhere, and I think I've come to realize why my parents spent the last seventeen years trying to keep me from it," her voice was so quiet, it was almost inaudible, "everything is so much, and I've been trying to tell myself it's okay, but it's not. I'm so scared."

"Hye, it's okay," he reassuring states, and as he says so, her teary eyes had finally looked to him, "I told you, I'm not going to let anything happen to you, I just need you to trust me."

She sniffles, trying hard to keep the tears from falling from her eyes, but they refused. He used his hand that wasn't holding hers to reach up, using the pad of his thumb to wipe them away. As he does so, she doesn't utter a word, and his fingers had went from under her eyes, to grazing across her soft, glass-like skin. They ran down her jawline, where he put two under her chin to force her to look at him again, "do you trust me?"

It took her a minute to find what she wanted to say, "of course I do."

A grin spreads over his lips at these words falling from her lips. Pulling her towards him, Hyeyeon's eyes widened as their proximity became closer than she had been planning. "Then don't push me away," his voice grew to a whisper as he looked down at her.

Their lips were only a mere few inches apart, and the anticipation was killing her. I can't, a part of her kept telling her, but another part wanted to so badly.

She didn't know, at the end of the day, she didn't know how she felt about Jay, or Jaemin. But she did know how her heart fluttered when she looked at Haechan.

"I'll find out who's after you, and when I do, I'm going to kill them," he hums in a low tone, his eyes tauntingly staring down into hers, "but first, Hye," he pauses, only increasing her desire to know what he was going to say next.

"What is it?"

"Let me kiss you."

So she did.

Every rule in her book, everything she had been telling herself for the last few years broke in that moment. One more look into his puppy like, shining eyes and she was sold, she couldn't take it anymore. Whether it was the teenage angst eating her insides or her feelings that she had been trying to push away the entire time, she wanted to do this.

It was why Hyeyeon had stepped only another inch forward to fully enclose the space between them. Haechan's eyes watch her movements, and already knowing what her answer was he lets go of her hand to full cup her cheeks so he can attach his lips to hers.

Unlike when she'd kissed him in the rain back at Sicheng's gang's house, this kiss was long. There was more meaning now that it wasn't just in the heat of the moment, it was fully intentional. Two teenagers who struggled throughout their lives, who found it hard to be true to their emotions, had finally found peace. Despite all the stressful things that they experienced and still would daily, they found the perfect thing to balance out that stress - each other.

His lips were softer than she could've imagined. They moved in a sweet melody with hers, creating an explosion of euphoria in her heart. Here she was, breaking all of her old promises to herself.

But she trusted him.

Her small hands go to his chest that's still covered by his white tee and still soaked from the rain, which she runs her hands down. The both of them were exhausted from the day, overwhelmed by all their emotions, but yet, as they pulled away they felt relieved.

Because after all this time, they'd finally been true to one thing.

"Haecha-," her words are cut off as she steps away from him, feeling out of breathe.

"You know, everything I said through our texts, I meant that," her eyes widen at these words, "I think we'd be great together."

In surprise, she had to turn away to hide the fact she was about to faint. Reaching up a hand, she runs it through her air, letting out an exasperated breathe as she tries to think about what he just said to her. No matter how hard she tried, it seemed to be difficult to get any of her thoughts straight.

Did she have feelings for Haechan? It was rather clear she did now. But did she have feelings for anyone else? She didn't know the answer to that one.

However, despite any of those thoughts, it was clear he felt strongly for her. And as much as she wouldn't mind being with him, as much as she wanted to, there was still something stopping her. It was like there was still another obstacle, something left that was keeping her from telling him what he wanted to hear.

At the same time, though, she couldn't find the words to tell him no.

Instead, she turns back to his expectant face, "can we talk about this another time? I don't feel well."

His face grows surprised at her saying this, "we can, don't worry about it," he walks closer to her in concern, "what's wrong?"

Hye only shakes her head, about to tell him she was just exhausted from the long day when a abrupt yawn had left her lips instead. The way she opened her mouth so widely made Haechan giggle as he raises a brow, "you should probably go to sleep."

She only nods, thinking of how badly she wanted to collapse on her soft bed. But she wasn't going without one thing.

Casually, she'd walked back over to him to grab his hand. Haechan was surprised as she'd begun dragging him away, but she knew he was letting her. If he didn't want her to, he would've easily been able to stop her.

"I was going to sleep on the couch, you know," he was saying as they were already going up the steps, but from the cheeriness evident in his tone when he spoke, she knew he'd wanted this all along.

Knowing this well, Hyeyeon rolls her eyes as she reaches her bedroom, "hey, you said you didn't want me to be alone!" she'd hummed defensively, letting his hand go once they'd entered her bedroom.

He'd only laughed in response, standing in the middle of her medium sized, carpeted room whilst she'd closed the door out of preference. Hyeyeon hadn't paid much attention due to the fact she was already falling asleep, and only walked to her bed before practically catapulting onto the mattress face first into the pillows.

The red haired boy was otherwise distracted by her walls. They were rather empty, except for a few band posters he didn't recognize, and a good amount of polaroids that were above her desk. It sat on the right side of her room, by the window that had the curtains closed over it to prevent any light from ever shining through.

His curiosity had got the best of him as he walked over, his eyes raking over the many photos that were mainly her and Sicheng. However, there were also some with a couple - who he presumed must be her parents. The only thing was, Hye was practically a child in any of the photos with them.

Although it hadn't been long enough to get that sort of information out of her, he realized he'd never heard her say a word about them. It raised the question in his brain, where are her parents?

It didn't seem like the guy back at the 127 house wanted anything to do with the gangs, either of them. He seemed only after Hye, after all, if it had something to do with them, wouldn't he have said so?

But he'd only stated her, how these people were only after her. And now that he really thought about it, the only thing it could have to do with was her family.

This was still a long shot for Haechan, because either way he knew nothing about them. But it did seem like they had a crazy amount of money, even for him. He could only wonder why she didn't have more designer clothing and a brand new car as his eyes glance back over to the girl, who was already fast asleep on her bed. As she slept, she looked content, still wearing his soaked valor jacket.

Chuckling at the sight of her, he'd just about to of walked over to lay beside her when he noticed something else, a polaroid camera. It sat just under all the photos on the wall atop the desk, seemingly calling out to him.

The temptation had been too real as he'd picked it up. Holding it out in front of him, Haechan made a large amount of ridiculous faces as he snapped endless photos of himself. Chuckling to himself as he watched them print out, he'd set them on her desk for her to find whenever she was sad.

Which he hoped she never was. More than anything, he aimed to protect her, and he would.

No matter what it took.

With that, he slowly climbs onto the bed beside her, being careful to still give her space so it wasn't too weird. He'd expected her to ask him exactly why he had been at the gang house, and Haechan had no doubt been dreading how he would explain that one. The story he was thinking of in his head was that he just followed them there because he was too worried about her, after all he said he wasn't going to leave her alone. It sounded pretty smart in his head, but he didn't know how it'd sound to her.

Donghyuck had also come to the conclusion he forgot or lost his phone back at the house. Truthfully, this wasn't much of a tragedy to him — now he had complete privacy and space away from the idiots back at the house.

For once, despite all the problems he was facing, Haechan felt content as he closed his eyes that night.

A sigh leaves his lips as he turns on his phone, realizing he had yet to check any of his notifications since he woke up.

Rubbing her eyes with her balled fists, Hyeyeon blinks in confusion as she peers around her bedroom. Slowly but surely, memories of last night flood into her brain like tsunami. Holding a hand to her head, she winces as she recalls it all.

The people who were after her for a reason she didn't know, the guy shooting himself at Cheng's house, but most of all what somehow made her want to scream the most — she kissed Haechan, or should she call him Donghyuck?

Throwing her feet over the side of the bed, she forces herself up. From what happened, a few aches reside in her body. There were no doubt bruises that formed along her legs and arms from being hit, and she could feel the effect as she limps down the stairs.

She should've looked out the window to see if Haechan's BMW was still parked, but she hadn't bothered. A part of her knew he wouldn't have left.

As soon as she reaches the bottom of the stairs in the usually dead silent house, the sound of Michael Jackson had filled her ears. Shaking her head, the question was answered for sure, that was the Donghyuck she knew and adored.

His candy like voice had filled her ears as he was singing along to Thriller like he was some sort of super star. The sound of the door swinging open to the kitchen had nearly made Haechan slip on the kitchen floor as he was doing some sort of dance along with it, and Hye couldn't held the inhuman snort of humor that left her mouth when she witnessed it.

Holding a hand to cover her mouth, she bursts into hysterics at the sight. Never would one have expected to see someone like Lee Haechan dancing to Michael Jackson, but here she was.

Donghyuck turns away as he tries to hide the pink that took over his cheeks. Recalling everything that had happened, he cleared his throat as he recollects himself, "how are you feeling? I hope that cheered you up."

Still giggling every few seconds, she slips into the booth of the kitchen table as she says in bewilderment, "yeah, yeah it did," she exhales, before speaking seriously, "but I'm alright, bruised up pretty bad but it's not lethal."

Pursing his lips, you could see the hint of embarrassment still written on his face as she pours another glass of water other than the one he was drinking. Walking over to the table, he slides into the booth next to her, setting the glass before her. "Are you sure it's just bruises?" He raises a brow, pending in concern, "do you need medicine?"

Before he could throw anymore questions of worry, she vigorously shakes her head, insisting, "no, it's okay, Hyuck, really."

He had to bite his lip to suppress the smile from hearing the name. It wasn't the time for him to get all fuzzy around a girl, even if it was Hyeyeon. There were much bigger things they had to worry about.

Clearing his throat, he looks away from the girl beside him who was casually drinking her water. He had been thinking hard on this before he was so rudely interrupted by the stupid group chat Jisung made. In the end, Haechan decided it was what he needed to know if he was ever going to get to the bottom of any of this.

So, gathering his courage, he asks hesitantly, "Hye, where are your parents?"

A lump is caught in her throat when such a question is thrown into the air. She hadn't expected to be asked this so early, but she guess she should've figured he would ask eventually.

She had been thinking about it, too. It was no lie that the man, and whoever else was after her, from yesterday hadn't mentioned a thing about 127 or Dream. He had only been focused on Hyeyeon and her only.

Whatever these people wanted with her, it wasn't because of her involvement with either of the gangs. It only left a limited amount of options, that incidentally all ended up pointing to one thing — her family.

Sighing, she caresses her temples as if to calm herself, feeling Hyuck's eyes boring holes into the side of her head. She peers straight ahead as she thinks, trying to decide exactly what to say.

"Uh, they're business folk, I guess," she finally mutters, "I never knew much about what business they do, though. They were home a lot more when I was younger, but my mom only ever told me it was something 'I wasn't old enough to understand'."

Donghyuck is in deep thought as she continues, trying to comprehend what he was hearing. "By the time I got older, they were here less often. My dad told me business was booming, so they were always having to go on business trips and stay for long amounts of time," she stares at her hands in her lap, seeming nervous to really be talking about all this. The only one who ever knew anything about it was Cheng — and Jisung, but she didn't want to think about him.

"The last time I saw them they told me I should always be careful," she recalls after another few seconds of silence, "they've told me that my whole life. It's why they always kept me secluded, even if I didn't listen when they weren't here."

By the end of her story, it all seemed to click in his head. Even though Hye didn't know what kind of 'business' her family was into, he was started to get a good feeling.

He knew exactly why they had to be after her, and no doubt it pinpointed to her family.

An exasperated sigh leaves the bleached blonde's lips. He runs a hand through his hair multiple times, pulling at the locks in immense frustration. There were so many worries crowding his mind, and as he looks up to his expectant gang members, he felt hopeless.

"Well, what's going on with your friend?" Yuri had asked, "does she need help?"

Leaning his head back in the sofa, he inhales the scent of smoke as he tries to sort through what's going on in his head.

"Yeah, they're after her because of her parents and something they're involved in that's probably illegal," he begins, "the body was whoever it was that tried to kidnap her, but he shot himself before he could get questioned."

Every one of his friends are staring at him like he went insane. There was an obvious piece of the puzzle missing, one he was dreading sharing with them even though he had to sooner or later.

"She took him on herself?" Johnny had gawked in surprise, "damn, I didn't think she was that feisty."

Receiving looks of disappoint from how that clearly wasn't true, Johnny had only ignored them as he continued to smoke the cigarette he was deeply invested in.

"We know there's more to the story," Doyoung advises when he sees the dull look on Win's face, "I'd recommend getting it out now."

Sicheng sighs as he sits up straight. His thoughts were so loud that he didn't hear the footsteps coming down the stairs behind him. The leader of 127 had appeared seconds later, the exact moment he breathed out, "Dream knows our location."

Taeyong's eyes grew red with anger at this. His fists clenched at his sides, and he could only sputter the word, hoping it was some sort of joke, "what?!"

Seeing that the leader was there, it made Cheng hate what was happening even more. He knew this was his fault, he was the one who so carelessly went to pick Hye up from their house. He should've known he was being followed, but Haechan was always good about these things. The boy had won the battle this time, and he was beyond upset with himself about it.

"Haechan followed me," he shamefully admits, "and he no doubt shared it with the rest of them."







///

Monday rolled around faster than anyone wanted. The entire weekend was horrible for the Dreamies. It was spent mourning their lost brother and feeling completely lost inside.

Eventually, Mark had told them they had to get over theirselves and move forward even when it hurt. If they were going to get back at a gang as experienced at 127, it would have to go out with a bang. There was no easy solution to this, and the death of their brother meant war.

Jisung had deemed to them that morning that he had a plan. Everyone was worried about what it could be, since it was showing recently that he wasn't very great at this entire thing. However, he had shown — on the other hand — that he was determined to avenge Jeno and would do whatever it took. It made them realize the reason they chose him as a leader back then.

School felt dewy, as news of Jeno's death had spread. Since all of the boys were well known and a lot of girls threw themselves at them, it wasn't just Dream that was affected by Jeno's passing.

"Everyone please proceed to the school yard to pay respects to our fellow classmate, Lee Jeno," the intercom had informed the students. It hadn't been long until everyone was filing outside of the school towards the yard, where staffs and Dream had set up a funeral for the beloved boy.

Meanwhile, Hyeyeon had stood idle in the middle of the hall. Students rushed passed her carelessly, for once not acknowledging her existence to make any rude comments. It was odd to her, but she couldn't complain, as she rakes her eyes over each of them, in search for either of the boys that were stuck on her mind.

Since she never got to hang out with Nana like she planned, she felt beyond bad about it. He was always so sweet to her and dealt with so much thanks to Jisung always wanting to mess with everyone. Even then, Jaemin had never been rude, and the two had yet to really talk about everything that had happened. She guessed that was why he wanted to hang out in the first place.

As for Haechan, she just wanted to ask how he was doing. She knew there was a lot going on, and when he was at her house all they talked about was the people that were after her. Hyeyeon had yet to really ask him about how he was coping with the loss of his dear friend — not to mention the feelings they were both burying because of all the burdens that kept showing up in their lives.

Sighing, she turns back to walk at the back of the crowd of students heading outside. If anything, Haechan and Nana were probably already at the funeral.

Hiking her bag up her shoulders further, the early November air had slapped her as she steps outside. The school yard wasn't far from the porch of the school, and in the distance she could see where everyone was.

Upon the green grass, there were many chairs set up in rows. Flowers were spread around every which way you looked, and stereo's were playing some of the boys favorite songs. There was a closed coffin upon a concrete slate that had probably been moved there, with flowers outlining the top. Then, right in front of it, was a giant portrait of the smiling boy, where many girls were seen crying and anyone was able to pay respects.

Standing on the porch, she squints a bit as she watches it from a distance. Hyeyeon had always hated Jisung's gang with how they framed her for Jisung's drug overdose and lied to him. She never got her ex boyfriend to believe what had really all taken place, and eventually, she just learned to live with the fact he would always hate her for something that wasn't true.

Even though they did such things, even though they weren't the nicest people, even though they did unthinkable illegal things she didn't want to think of, they were still people. She couldn't deny the fact they felt human emotion, and that they found family in each other. No doubt it hurt them to lose one of their fellow members, and at the sight of them all hugging each other, tears pouring down their cheek as they stood around the boy's coffin — she realized that.

Hyeyeon adored Donghyuck. She thought he was horrible at the beginning when she first heard of his mere existence. But after getting to know him, he was everything she would've never expected him to be — and now look at where they've come.

So, just maybe, the others were the same way. Maybe they weren't so bad, especially if Haechan still cared for them so deeply.

Jisung was another story. She knew he hated him, but wasn't sure why. Even then, there might be a way to fix that, too.

This didn't mean Hyeyeon still didn't hate Park Jisung. He put her through endless amounts of pain the last years. The entire school of DMHS hated her because of him and his friends, after all.

But she felt bad for what they were going through, and it made her realize that she might be able to put things behind her.

Staring a bit harder the group of boys, she noticed something she wasn't sure could be true. After a second of concentration, she realized there was no other explanation on who it could be.

Na Jaemin was with Dream, but she didn't get why. Last she checked, Jisung didn't seem to like him, right? Why was he hanging out with them?

Trying to understand and craving for something help her do such, she holds onto her bag as she begins to make her way through the grass. Students had stared at her as she passes them, finally seeming to remember she existed.

Ignoring anything they were saying that were along the lines of did you hear? She's messing with Jaemin and Donghyuck now. I can't believe they'd fall for her lies. Hyeyeon keeps her head high, her green eyes set on one group of boys and one group of boys only.

Lee Donghyuck had been sitting on his phone, trying to debate on if he wanted to text her or not. They hadn't really talked since he left her house the other day, after him endlessly insisting that she shouldn't be alone. Hyeyeon refused to listen until she practically shoved him out of her house, bidding that she would see him at school. He'd been worrying about her since. But he had yet to gather the courage to text her, being too busy battling his own emotions and working with the rest of his members to decide what they were going to do to avenge their brother.

At the sight of the girl who had been on his mind the entire weekend, his brown irises brighten. Many girls had come up to him through out the school day, trying to tell him about the rumors that had spread about her messing with him and Jaemin at the same time. But because he knew the truth, he pushed them all off.

However, the other boy who was questionably turning into the possible new recruit in Dream, had also saw the girl approaching. Neither of them were very fond of each other, and Haechan couldn't believe that they were considering just letting Jaemin in like that.

"Hyeyeon!" Jaemin calls out brightly before Haechan could, and the girl offers him a wave as she stops before him. She hadn't seemed to of noticed Haechan, weirdly enough.

"Nana," she offers a small smile, glancing around to the other members of Dream that were busy in a huddle, talking about something she didn't know, "I never thought I'd see you over here."

Knowing she was referring to him being around them, Jaemin scratches the back of his neck, "yeah, it's kind of hard to explain, it's part of what I need to talk to you about."

Pursing her lips in thought for a second, she nods after a moment, "oh, of course, sorry about the other day."

The sweet angel only waved it off, "don't worry about it! It's not your fault that something came up."

If only you knew, Nana.

"Yeah, a little more than just something," she sighs out, and sensing the clear distress in her voice, Nana raises an eyebrow, urging her to continue further. "I'll tell you in private," she assures.

Jaemin is about to suggest that they could go talk somewhere quiet, like the school garden, before the funeral. When suddenly, a boy that wasn't Haechan had stepped out from the huddle. His eyes were unusually welcoming as they land on the girl, and he offers an enthusiastic greeting, "hi Hyeyeon, nice to see you!"

Haechan was finally visible to her as the group had stepped back from their crowd where they were discussing 127 once again. Hyeyeon's eyes went from the Harry Potter boy who just said hello so casually to her, to Hyuck, back and forth as she tried to understand what was happening.

Seeming to read the look in her eyes, Haechan mouths, give him a chance.

Clearing her throat, she looks back to the boy, "uh, hi —," she pauses, realizing she didn't know his name.

"— Chenle, I'm Chenle," he informs her, before motioning to the uninterested boy beside him that just walked up, "and this is Renjun!"

Right, she mentally recalls to years prior, that's their names.

Still not understanding what was going on and why Hyuck had mouthed such a thing to her, she hesitantly responds, "good to know."

From the awkward tension, Renjun had started snickering as he buries his face in his hands, "Chenle, I told you this was fucking stupid, this is so weird!"

Hyeyeon blinks at them, about to speak up and ask for some clarification. When the feeling of someone's close presence is felt behind her.

"They realized they're fucking idiots so they're trying to make up for it," Haechan's voice breaks through the silence, "so, the right thing to say here would be I'm sorry for lying and making your life a living hell," he hums sternly, looking to the two boys before him expectantly.

Upon hearing this, Renjun rolls his eyes, not seeming like he really wanted to be a part of any of this. Hyeyeon turns to look back at Haechan, who was too busy glaring at the two to meet her gaze.

Turning back to them, Chenle had cleared his throat as he begins, "right, me and Renjun would like to apologize about that," he elbows the boy beside him, "actually, it was his idea, and I told him it wasn't very nice — but we sort of went with it anyway."

Realizing there was no getting out of this with the way Hyuck was staring them down with that harsh gaze of his, Renjun heaves out a sigh, "I was trying to come up with a way to break you guys up, and I figured this was the best one, since it fit with the accidental overdose and everything."

"Yeah, we wanted to recruit Jisung, but you were making that sorta hard."

She looks from boy to boy as she tries to really take it all in. The last thing she thought she would be hearing about today was this.

"Uh," she coughs a bit, not knowing what she should say. Although she was thinking about putting it all behind her earlier, was she really going to do that? Just like this?

She guessed that even though it was their idea to frame her with the drug overdose, they weren't really what she had a problem with. The one who did it all, who made her life a living hell, went by the name of Park Jisung.

So, after thinking about it, she gradually nods, "it's okay, I accept your apology."

"Really?!" Chenle had cried, "that's great!"

She was shocked to see how cheerful this guy was. Was he seriously in a gang?

"Cool, now I'm going to go focus on the fact that my friend is fucking dead," Renjun mumbles as he spins on his heel, before heading to where Jisung was gathered around the coffin.

Feeling a bit bad from how down he looked, she remembered why she walked over here in the first place.

"Sorry about your friend," she tells Chenle and Haechan, who were now the ones closest to her other than Nana, but she knew he had no relation to Jeno.

From the sudden mention, Chenle had cleared his throat. He turns away as tears well in his eyes, and she feels her heart break a bit at the sight.

"It's okay," his voice is barely above a whisper, "but I should go pay my respects, too," he sighs, looking to the sky as he forces himself to blink away tears. Just as he's walking away, he glances back to Hyuck, "and you should, too, Haechan."

"Yeah, go ahead, we can talk later," Hyeyeon pats his arm when she saw him staring at the coffin where everyone was gathered longingly.

There's a hesitant look in his eyes when he faces her again. They wander from her, to Jaemin, that was standing a bit behind her. Jaemin's eyes meet his gaze when they shift to him, and there's a glare in them that he knew well of.

Even if Hyeyeon didn't know yet, it wouldn't be long until Jaemin told her. And Hyuck already knew it well.

Knowing he had bigger problems on his hands, he nods as he sends her a soft smile, "I'll see you later, Hyeyeon."



Chapter thirty eight; heartfelt

"It's been a while since we've actually gotten to talk," the caramel haired boy hums into the peaceful atmosphere. The only sound after his words had fluttered away with the slight breeze blowing was the rustling of tree leaves above them. Although it was winter, there were still flowers that grasped for life in the school garden, being of many different colors that shone under the sun beaming down onto them through the tree branches they walked under.

Rocks and sticks crinkle under their feet as they walk. "Yeah, we really haven't gotten to since Halloween," Hyeyeon states the obvious. Nana had stopped before a bench that sat in the middle of the garden, and Hye followed him as took a seat.

There's a glisten in those eyes of his as he stared up at the scenery they were surrounded by. At first glance, it might seem like the two teenagers felt awkward from their lack of conversation, but it was actually the complete opposite. In reality, they'd just missed each other's presence so much so that they were still taking the time to take in the fact they had time alone after so long.

"About that night," he clears his throat suddenly, causing Hyeyeon's eyes to jolt to him from peering around at the flowers. A nervous look is hidden in his brown irises, that he blinks away as he meets her own, "I'm still sorry about it, I can't really remember anything now, I just know I got really mad at Jisung because I saw something was happening to you." Heaving out a long sigh, he rubs his temples as if to calm his nerves, muttering in frustration, "it must've been that stupid punch."

Pursing her lips in a straight line, a comfortable silence overcomes the two once again. Seeing that Jaemin was trying hard to recall the events of the party, she turns to face the garden as she does the same.

But it didn't matter how hard or how many times she racked her brain for some sort of remembrance, there was none. All she could recollect, just like when she woke up at Haechan's, was her leaving the house with Jaemin. She could vividly see when they got there and entered the gym, but after that, it became a fuzzy cloud of nothing.

It was like someone had ripped the entire portion of the party out of her brain. Looking back to Nana, he seemed to be having the same problem. Growing confused, she pends the question, wondering as to why his memory seemed to blank, "you drank the punch, too?"

Heaving out a deep breathe, he taps his fingers against his knee as he continues to ponder hard. Upon hearing Hye's question, he shakes his head, "not really, I don't know." His words came out in complete distress, he sounded like he was about to burst from the fact he couldn't recall much other than him getting mad at Jisung because she seemed to be in pain.

Why?

Why couldn't he remember anything? He hadn't had more than a sip of that punch, and it wasn't like it could've affected him from something so small.

"Do you remember the part about that Jeno guy?"

"Uh, sort of," he blinks in thought, his voice a mutter, "I didn't see his face clearly, but I figured it was him because I saw him walk out the gym that way, and he and the rest of Jisung's are the only people I know who'd be likely to have someone after them."

He never saw his face, and if he did, he couldn't remember it at all. It was funny, Jaemin's memory hadn't seemed like it was so fuzzy after the fact. Only until now, when he was actually trying to think about it had he realized.

"Weird," Hyeyeon mumbles, just as lost as he was, "that whole night was weird, I wonder why they were after him anyway."

He shrugs, "I don't know really either, something to do with another gang they're rivaling with."

She hadn't put two and two together. There were too many groups in a place like Chicago for her to immediately think the rivalry gang had to be the one her best friend was in. Instead, another thing strikes in her brain, and she sits up straight, shifting to face Nana on the bench they sat on, "well, don't bother yourself about remembering it anymore. It happened, and honestly, thinking about it freaks me out," she trembles at the thought of what happened days ago. Just thinking about how the guy had so openly shot himself made her feel sick to the stomach, but that night also made her think of something else; Donghyuck.

Hyuck, she really liked his real name. A guilty smile finds it's way on her face when she recalls how his lips felt atop hers, and only when Nana had cleared his throat had she been knocked out of her trance.

"Maybe the others remember something," he suggests, before hesitantly posing, "but uh, Yeonnie, did you find out exactly who did it since it wasn't Jisung?"

A lump forms in her throat from the question, and she swallowed it as she met his soft eyes that were pooling with concern. Seeing how abruptly stunned she looked from him asking, he hurriedly rushes to assure her, "it's okay, if you don't want to talk about it, please don't rush yourself," he sends her a bright grin to try to cheer her up, "I just worry about you."

For some reason, she feels heat rise to her cheeks. Hyeyeon breaks their eye contact, turning her head away to stare ahead at the flowers instead of meeting Jaemin's soft eyes.

"You're sweet, Nana," she gushes after a second of thought, her words sincere before her voice grew quiet compared to the soft breeze that blew, "it just all scares me."

Jaemin frowns at the sight of how distressed she appeared to be. He didn't know what exactly was happening, and he didn't want to pressure her to tell him everything either. A part of him felt bad that he had to find out what happened with her and Jisung from them and not Hyeyeon herself, but he guessed that was one less painful conversation they had to have.

Thinking quick on a way to comfort the poor girl lost in her own head, his hand reaches out and falls atop of her own before he could stop himself. She'd been resting her hands on either side of her on the bench, and when his own engulfs hers, he feels how cold she was thanks to the November air.

Hyeyeon jumps from the sudden feeling, but she doesn't move.

"I'm sorry," he soothes in a sympathetic voice, it was dripping of so much care she could almost melt under his gaze, "I wish there was something more I could do, I really want to help."

"Nana, are you working with them?"

Her abrupt question caused a look of confusion to wash over him, "huh?"

Exhaling slowly, she pauses before rephrasing what she asked, "Jisung's gang, are you working with them now? I won't be mad, I mean, I guess they're not terrible since they said sorry for lying about everything," she sighs, running the hand that wasn't covered by Jaemin's through her hair, "I still can't stand Jisung, though, I don't think we could ever be friends."

"Well, sort of, but it's kind of against my will," he explains, and she looks to him again with curious eyes.

"Yeah, I've heard you and Jisung go way back, don't you?" she raises a brow inquisitively, "so you knew him before he went haywire, too, huh?"

He chuckles at the way she tended to word things. "You could say that, but we were just childhood friends before he moved," Jaemin hums.

She nods in understanding, breaking their eye contact once again to stare at the flowers. Jaemin had noticed she'd been staring at a particular purple colored flower, one he didn't know the name of since he wasn't necessarily educated in such a thing. It seemed like she liked the flower though, and he made sure to make a mental note.

The quiet air was peaceful, and Hyeyeon closes her eyes as she just breathes in the joyous aura for once. It was nice, to be sitting in the garden with Nana, the only 'normal' person she really knew. Although she feared that would be changing soon with him getting involved with Jisung, but she didn't blame him.

None of them were normal anyway, not even her. She was more involved than anyone, so who was she to judge?

His hand was warm as it sat on hers, and she didn't mind the feeling. He's not Hyuck, but he was Jaemin, someone she adored in a way she didn't know how to compare for the feeling she felt with Haechan. It was better, in her complicated mind, to not think about it.

"Yeonnie," she screeched when Jaemin had laid his head on her shoulder in the middle of her deep thinking session, sing-songing her name like that of a child as he peered up to her with those big brown eyes, "I've gotta tell you something."

Trying to ignore the fact she wanted to scream from the feeling of his breathe fanning her skin, she asks in curiosity, a smile hinting on her face from how baby like he was, "yes, Nana?"

A few seconds pass, and her words seem to float away into the atmosphere. Jaemin doesn't reply for a minute or two, raising a mass of confusion on if he was ignoring her or just didn't hear her.

"If you could have anything in the world, what would it be?"

She blinks in shock from his question. He'd sat up from laying on her shoulder, turning to cross his legs over each other and face her on the bench. She does the same so she could see if he was seriously asking her such a thing. Sure enough, his expression didn't show a sign of any joking manner.

Looking to the trees above them in thought, she ponders for a bit. In Hyeyeon's mind, she tried to not think about the hardships in her personal life. The main thing that would mean is her parents, they were the last thing she ever allowed to be on her mind.

It sucked not having them around for nearly your entire life. They were apparently such well known business people, but she never even knew what business they ran. Never had they told her a thing about it, always insisting she was too young. The way they kept her trapped in the house and guarded growing up had only made it worse. She only ever got to go out when they left on their trips, but when they were home, she barely ever got to leave her room.

As a kid, she just thought they were protective. Looking at it now, she could understand that the city of Chicago was a dangerous place. But it seemed like there was something more they wanted to keep her from, and she was just now facing it.

Haechan's theory wasn't far fetched at all.

So, the everlasting question, what did she want most in the world?

A real family.

"A dog," she blurts unexpectedly, and Nana furrows his brows as he stares at her completely serious expression.

He didn't think she would say that out of all things. It was a pretty deep question, most people would've answered something like world peace or whatever; but he guessed he was glad it was simple.

"A dog?" he repeats, and she enthusiastically nods, a childish grin on her lips, "out of everything you could have you want a dog? What kind of dog?"

"Yeah, my parents are always on trips so it gets kind of lonely at my house," she explains, "a dog would be fun to have to keep me company," thinking about the breed excited her as she leans forward. Not knowing what she was doing until it was too late, she grabbed both of Nana's hands as she meets his eyes joyously, "have you ever heard of a samoyed? They're seriously the cutest thing I've ever seen."

There's already a smile finding it's way onto his face. Her hands were so small as they barely covered his, so he shifts the way they were holding hands, engulfing hers with his on top instead. A pout forms on his lips as he tries to mask the cutest voice he could manage, "aw, I'm not the cutest thing you've ever seen?" he whined playfully.

Rolling her eyes, she disconnects one of their hands to poke his cheek with her pointer finger. "You're a close second, Nana, dogs come first."

The caramel boy giggles like a kid, and it makes her cheeks turn pink again. She hated how it kept happening, with the way his eyes would sparkle under the sunlight peeking through the trees. Na Jaemin was getting to her all over again, and she didn't know how to stop it.

As if that wasn't enough, the worst part was Lee Donghyuck was getting to her just as badly.

"I guess I can live with that," he dramatically sighs.

He'd grabbed her hand again when she wasn't paying full attention. Jaemin's thumbs rub circles on her knuckle as he sees she was thinking hard about something for a second, and he broke her thoughts as he blurts out what was on his mind, "you're pretty cute, too, Yeonnie."

Air got caught in her throat from the words, and she coughed a bit as her head jolts back to him, "huh - oh, t-thanks," she stuttered like an idiot. Hyeyeon wanted to punch herself from how dumb she just sounded, but she forces a smile on her face to hide it.

More silence.

Jaemin really wanted to tell her. He wanted to tell her a lot, all the way from what Jisung's friends had told him about her past to the fact that he couldn't hold it in anymore. Jaemin couldn't hold his feelings in anymore.

Maybe the thing about him knowing her past wasn't so important. If she ever tried to tell him he would explain to her about it then that he already knew. As far as he was concerned, it wasn't something he thought about. The past, and whatever Jisung thought Hyeyeon was such a bad person for, didn't define her in his eyes.

Since he was human, a part of him wondered what the real thing Jisung spoke about when he says she wasn't innocent. He understood that apparently Hyeyeon had broken up with him that night when he was having trouble, but that didn't make it her fault he did that to himself. It didn't mean she deserved all the pain they had put her through, making the entire school hate her for something so silly like a break up.

Although, he was still curious if that was the full story. But it wasn't what he wanted to tell her first.

Gathering his courage, Na Jaemin's heart was on his shoulders as he exhales, gripping her small hands in his own tighter, "Yeonnie, listen—"

"—Hyeyeon!"
